Local News

Wang Jingwei Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Morning

Still Humbly Declined the Position of Premier

Wang Said He Came to Shanghai to Visit Soong and Urge Him to Take the Post

And Telegraphed the Central Government Requesting Soong's Formal Appointment

Soong's Attitude Was Resolute, Still Urging Wang to Resume His Post

Premier Wang Jingwei, accompanied by his wife, Ms. Chen Bijun, and the Vice Minister of Railways, Zeng Zhongming, and others, arrived in Shanghai by night train from Nanjing the night before last at 11:00 PM. Yesterday morning at 7:50 AM, he got off the train at Zhenru Station and went straight back to his residence on Pushi Road to rest. Wang stated that he came to Shanghai to meet with Acting Premier Soong Ziwen and ask Soong to formally assume the post of Premier. After Soong agrees, Wang will immediately return to Nanjing, schedule a trip to the north to comfort the soldiers at the front, and meet with Military Affairs Committee Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. Otherwise, he intends to stay in Shanghai temporarily, expressing his determination. After Wang got off the train, he telegraphed the Central Standing Committee, proposing to formally appoint Soong as Premier. Details are as follows:

Got off at Zhenru

A reporter from this newspaper drove to Zhenru Station at about 7:00 AM yesterday morning. At that time, there was no one in the station except the staff, and there was no arrangement for armed military police or security teams to be on strict guard. At about 7:40 AM, Wang's secretary arrived at the station to greet him. At 7:50 AM, the train arrived at the station, and Wang and his wife and Zeng Zhongming got off the train and went straight back to his residence on Pushi Road to rest.

Wang's Remarks

When Wang got off the train at Zhenru Station, he was wearing a gray suit, and his complexion was rosy and his spirits were good. A reporter from this newspaper immediately stepped forward to talk to him. According to Wang, regarding the issue of the Premier, he was determined to resign because his body had not fully recovered and it was difficult to cope with the demanding tasks. Today, the Central Standing Committee will formally discuss this matter. He has telegraphed requesting the appointment of Mr. Soong Ziwen as Premier. This time, he came to Shanghai to meet with Mr. Soong and urge him to take the post. After Soong agrees, he will return to Nanjing within days, and then schedule a trip to the north to comfort the soldiers at the front and meet with Military Affairs Committee Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. Otherwise, he will stay in Shanghai temporarily and wait for the resolution of this matter.

Personally Visited Soong Ziwen

At 9:30 AM, Wang went to Soong's residence in a light car with a simple entourage. He earnestly expressed to Soong that he was unable to cope with the demanding tasks due to his illness, and requested that he reluctantly agree to take the post of Premier. However, Soong still humbly declined, saying that his physical strength was also weak and his blood pressure was still high, so he resolutely refused to take office and refused to act as an agent again. The two men negotiated for 30 minutes, still humbly declining each other, and there was no result in the end. Wang then resigned.

Zeng Zhongming Said

According to Zeng Zhongming, the Vice Minister of Railways who accompanied Wang to Shanghai, Mr. Wang refused to resume his post because his body could not support the demanding tasks. This time he came to Shanghai to persuade Mr. Soong to come to Nanjing to do the real thing in order to avoid mistakes and harm the country. After Wang resigned from the post of Premier, he did not completely ignore state affairs and would serve in the Central Party Headquarters. As for whether Wang will return to Nanjing immediately, it depends on the situation of his contact with Vice Premier Soong. The Central Committee held a standing meeting this morning to discuss this matter. If this matter is resolved, Mr. Wang can enter Nanjing in one or two days. If Soong still declines, the Central Committee has no intention of recommending anyone else. The time for Wang and Chiang to meet has not yet been determined. All parties intend to recommend Mr. Chiang to be the Commander-in-Chief of the Army, Navy, and Air Force in order to unify military power. I have not heard anything about this in Nanjing. I will return to Nanjing by night train tonight.

Telegram to the Central Government

After Wang arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning, he telegraphed the Central Committee, proposing to the Central Standing Committee to formally appoint Acting Premier Soong as Premier. The original text read, "To the Central Executive Committee, Jian: Last year in August, Zhaoming resigned from the post of Premier. The Central Committee decided to order him to concentrate on serving in the Central Party Headquarters, and Vice Premier Soong Ziwen was appointed as Acting Premier. In mid-October, Kuang Zhaoming applied for leave because his illness was serious and he could not serve in the Central Party Headquarters. He was granted leave for three months to go to Europe for treatment. Recently, with the fall of Rehe, he rushed back to Nanjing despite his illness, hoping to share this difficulty with his comrades. However, at this time, he can only do his best and contribute at any time in the Central Party Headquarters. As for the post of Premier, the matter is complicated and the responsibility is heavy. The sick body is not worth cherishing, but harming the country by incurring debts is a deep fault. Since entering Nanjing, he has repeatedly explained this in detail to his comrades, hoping to gain their understanding. This morning is the date of the Central Standing Committee meeting. He dares to sincerely appeal and respectfully asks for understanding and to determine Comrade Soong Ziwen as Premier, cancel the word 'acting', in order to specialize in responsibility and listen to one opinion. As long as Zhaoming has one breath left, he will still follow his comrades in the Central Party Headquarters to face the national crisis together. This proposal is respectfully submitted, awaiting public decision."

Song Ziwen's Firmness

A reporter visited Song Ziwen, the Acting President of the Executive Yuan, at 10:30 yesterday morning. According to Song, Mr. Wang (Jingwei) came this morning and indicated that he would not be returning to his original position as President of the Executive Yuan, and instructed me to continue in that responsibility. However, I firmly stated that I could not take on the role, so that I can specialize in finance. The position of President of the Executive Yuan should naturally be returned to Mr. Wang. At this time of increasing national crisis, if the entire country unanimously urges Mr. Wang, he should be able to reluctantly take on the difficult task and jointly overcome the national crisis. Regarding the central government's policy towards Japan, it is determined to resolutely resist and never compromise. Rumors from the outside suggesting direct negotiations and compromise with Japan are not factual, which is very clear. Japan cannot even accept the resolutions of the League of Nations, and is even considering withdrawing from the League. How is there any possibility they would concede to us? And would our government be willing to submit to a powerful enemy and sign a treaty that would ruin the nation? In any case, anyone who compromises with Japan will certainly be spurned by the entire country. Regarding the military situation in North China, I (Song referring to himself) have no special insights. I only know that the troop movements in Ludong are purely for strategic necessity. The Japanese are spreading rumors that they will disrupt Tianjin and Beijing, and we are also prepared. If the enemy recklessly invades Tianjin and Beijing, they will certainly be met with a fierce counterattack. Recently, various parties have recommended Chairman Chiang Kai-shek as the Commander-in-Chief of the Army, Navy, and Air Force, to unify authority. However, Chairman Chiang himself only seeks military success in resisting the enemy, and does not seek to take on the title.

Chu Discusses Wang's Medical Treatment

A Central News Agency dispatch from Nanjing on the 23rd reported that Premier Wang (Jingwei) and his wife, Ms. Chen Bijun, and Tieci Zeng Zhongming, etc., traveled to Shanghai by night train on the 22nd, as reported in the newspapers. A Central News Agency reporter visited Chu Minyi at the Executive Yuan on the morning of the 23rd, inquiring about when Wang would return to Nanjing. Chu replied that since Wang has returned to the country, travel between Nanjing and Shanghai is a common occurrence for various ministers and committee members. As far as I know, this trip to Shanghai is perhaps for medical treatment and blood tests, as drawing blood from a vein for examination is difficult for ordinary doctors. Dr. Nauer, who accompanied Wang to Europe before, also returned to Shanghai with Wang, so Wang is still seeking his diagnosis and treatment.

Yu Mingzhou Speaks

Applying the Full-Line Attack Plan to Resist Japan

Also Discussing the Hope for Aid to Launch Hidden Righteous Armies

Yesterday Accompanying Wu Huanzhang to Visit Mayor Wu

Yu Mingzhou, the Heilongjiang Party Affairs Guidance Committee member and Deputy Commander of the Heilongjiang People's Self-Defense Army, and Li Mingxin, the representative of Pu Bingshan and Deng Wen, have successively come to Shanghai to contact various organizations in the city for assistance. Yu spoke with a reporter from the New Voice Society at his residence yesterday, as follows:

Because of Our Local Resistance

The Japanese army uses powerful, modern weapons to carry out invasions, but the combat capabilities of their soldiers are extremely weak and not worth a single blow. As seen in the Battle of Nenjiang, the Battle of Shanghai, and the recent Battle of Xifengkou, our army inflicted heavy damage on them. However, the Japanese are using a strategy of defeating each enemy individually, and our country has fallen into the error of local resistance, resulting in successive defeats in Shanghai and the provinces of Jilin and Heilongjiang. With the loss of Yuguan and the invasion of Rehe, the Japanese have been able to advance leisurely and do whatever they want without any scruples. Now they are pressing on the Great Wall. We must learn from the past and determine that resistance alone is not enough.

Being Defeated by the Japanese Individually

The troops that the Japanese army has recently used to invade Rehe are mostly transferred from the provinces of Jilin and Heilongjiang. Three brigades, such as the Suzuki brigade, have fought with our army in Heilongjiang. From the records examined on the bodies of captured enemy soldiers in the battles in Heilongjiang, it is known that most of them participated in the Battle of Shanghai. According to statistics, the Japanese army occupying the four northeastern provinces numbers less than 100,000, which is far fewer than our army. However, due to the result of local resistance, they invaded Shanghai in the south, and after the ceasefire, they were transferred to the Northeast, successively defeating the units of Pu Bingshan, Su Bingwen, Ma Zhanshan, Wang Delin, Feng Zhanhai, and Li Du. They then launched a full-scale invasion of Rehe. The righteous armies in Jilin and Heilongjiang, due to traffic obstruction, cannot connect with each other and act together, leading to their individual defeat. Now the battleground has reached the Great Wall, and the equipment of the central armies is far superior to that of the civilian uprisings. If local resistance is still used, fighting back only where the enemy breaks through, then its future is truly precarious. A plan for a full-line attack should be devised quickly, so that the Japanese army cannot cope, and this is the only way to recover the lost territories.

Huge Quantities of Russian Goods Imported

According to yesterday's Japanese-language Shanghai Daily, since the resumption of diplomatic relations between China and Russia, various goods from the Soviet Union have been continuously transported to China and distributed to cities and markets throughout China, with Shanghai as the center. The important goods being dumped include timber, kerosene, calico, coal, glass, wheat, and fish. An inspection of the import goods of the third ship in the Russian merchant fleet, the Kedsk, on the 21st showed the following: (1) 5,000 tons of kerosene, with a total value of approximately 20 million taels. These goods have been unloaded at the 16th Bund wharf. Except for timber and coal, which are directly managed by Russian merchants, the kerosene is sold by Guanghua Company, and the calico is managed by Da Zhonghua Company.

Mayor Wu's Radio Address Yesterday

How Should Citizens Save China?

Mayor Wu gave a radio address at the Chinese and Western Drugstore Radio Station, arranged by the Bureau of Education, at 7 PM last night, titled "How Should Citizens Save China?" The following is a transcript of his speech:

Ladies and gentlemen, at this time when the life of our nation is in extreme danger and our beautiful land is shrinking day by day, as Japanese troops invade our borders, after rushing about in alarm, being filled with intense emotion, and being in a state of grief and worry, have the people of our entire nation also quietly observed and thought deeply about what caused this unprecedented national crisis? Have you also considered how to rise up and strengthen ourselves to avoid the immense terror of the future and overcome this unprecedented crisis? Have you also considered how to wipe out our shame and strive for strength, how to shoulder the responsibility of saving the nation and resisting foreign aggression, and how to restore the glorious history of our nation? From the perspective of the situation of the entire world, the current situation of China, and the principles of human survival, at this moment, we naturally only have "active resistance" to open up a path for our nation. Moreover, only by working together in harmony, gathering the strength of the nation, and uniting to save the country can we save this unprecedented misfortune and develop new opportunities for the revival of our nation. However, our country has historically been an excellent cultured nation. In terms of population, territory, climate, resources, and all the elements that constitute a nation, we are above other countries. Why are we being invaded and trampled upon? When we are resisting and fighting, if we do not first think deeply about this point and consider why other countries are strong and reflect on why our country has declined, we will not be able to establish a great plan for saving the country and reveal the path to struggle. If everyone only knows blind patriotism and superficial struggle, and does not save the country in the right way or struggle with the right strength, then the result of resistance and struggle will certainly not harm the powerful enemy. In around 1806, after Germany was defeated by Napoleon, an patriotic philosopher, Fichte, gave a speech to their citizens, saying, "We have now been conquered, but whether we will suffer the humiliation of the enemy again and whether we will never be able to restore the glory of the nation all depends on our own determination and our own efforts." "Everyone should know that Germany's failure is not the fault of one or two people, but the common fault of the people of the whole country. It is the result of the ignorance, confusion, immaturity, cowardice, and various morbidities of the people of the whole country. The war of force has now passed. The war from now on is a war of knowledge, a war of morality, and a war of character. Whether we can participate in this kind of war also depends on whether our citizens have the determination." What I hope from the listeners is that you do not seek temporary comfort, do not be complacent, do not be passive, and do not simply engage in grief and indignation. You should engage in thorough thinking and find ways to free yourselves from suffering. "The value of our lives lies in the eternal life of our nation. If the nation dies, we are dead even if we are alive. If the nation lives, we are alive even if we are dead. Therefore, we should sacrifice and fight for the life of the nation." China's situation today is the same as Germany's at that time, and Fichte's speech to the German people is equal to a speech to our citizens. It is very worthy of our citizens' reference and reflection. However, the German nation has been transformed and has become strong after being influenced by Fichte's speech, but the Chinese people have been subjected to the aggression and oppression of the great powers for a hundred years and still cannot awaken and cannot become strong. This cannot but be said to be the greatest weakness and crisis in the spirit of our nation. Now, the general public all know the term "national crisis," but how many people truly understand the meaning of the national crisis and the causes of the national crisis? How many people are truly able to save the country in a practical way? Everyone should know that "worry is enough to revitalize a country." The external troubles of enemy countries are not a national crisis, and military aggression is not enough to destroy a country. Only the self-degeneration of a nation is the greatest crisis and the cause of the nation's demise. If the national spirit can be united and uplifted, and if the national will can be strengthened and developed, then the foundation of the country can naturally be consolidated and the nation can naturally develop. Now, the greatest danger in China is that the general public still does not know the true meaning of the country and the causes of the national crisis, and that those who lead the public to save the country only know how to engage in superficial enthusiasm and cannot make practical efforts. Therefore, in the past hundred years, although there have been national salvation movements after every national crisis, every national salvation movement has failed to save China. We enlightened people should learn from our pain and, from now on, thoroughly recognize the meaning of the national crisis, reflect on the causes of the national crisis, and know that the arrival of the national crisis is not the result of one morning or evening, nor is it the fault of one or two people, but the common fault of the people of the whole country, and it is the result of the long-term accumulation of evils such as ignorance, confusion, immaturity, cowardice, apathy, selfishness, complacency, and laziness of the people of the whole country. Going forward, we should deeply reproach ourselves, strive to become new, be down-to-earth, and make a firm and determined resolution to work hard, be brave, and save the country, starting from culture, economics, everyone's job, and the way of life in peacetime, working hard and realistically to enrich the content of the nation's life and consolidate the foundation for national development. Every effort we make is one point of national salvation, and the sum total of the efforts of the people of the whole country is the final success of the nation's wiping out its shame and striving for strength. The ancients said, "Ten years of breeding, ten years of teaching." Wiping out shame and striving for strength cannot be achieved overnight, but must wait for long-term and practical efforts to take effect. It is hoped that the people of the whole country will abide by this iron law of saving the country, recognize the crux of the current national crisis, determine a long-term struggle policy, and make real efforts to cope with this unprecedented and drastic world change and restore the inherent glory and splendor of our great cultured Chinese nation. If, at this critical moment of life and death, we make mistake after mistake and cannot open a path to survival and struggle for survival, then the tragedy of national subjugation and the catastrophe of racial extermination may be in the near future.

Yunnan Fellow Provincials in Shanghai

Meeting to Discuss Purchasing Airplanes

The Yunnan Chamber of Commerce Sends Representatives to Shanghai to Assist

The Kunming Chamber of Commerce in Yunnan Province, considering that Yunnan Province is located in a remote area with inconvenient transportation and that its industry and commerce have not developed, especially at this time of economic competition and promotion of domestic goods, believes that it is necessary to quickly find ways to improve industry and commerce in order to prevent capital outflow. The Chamber has sent Ma Chunlong, a standing committee member and director of the general affairs section of the Chamber, to major cities such as Beijing, Tianjin, Shanghai, and Wuhan to conduct thorough investigations in order to learn from them how to improve industry and commerce. Mr. Ma passed through Hong Kong and arrived in Shanghai on the 18th of this month. On the 21st, he met with Wang Xiaolai, the chairman of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, and was guided by Zhu Boyuan, the director of the National Products Market, to visit the National Products Exhibition Hall and the National Products Market. The Chamber of Commerce also sent letters to major factories in the city, introducing Mr. Ma to visit and conduct inspections. It is reported that Mr. Ma plans to complete his investigations in Shanghai and then travel to Beijing, Wuhan, and other places to continue his work.

Also reported, various groups in Yunnan Province, due to the increasing national crisis, have elected representatives to organize the Yunnan People's National Salvation Association, with the aim of concentrating the financial and human resources of the entire province, assisting the government, preparing for national defense, and resisting foreign aggression. They have appointed Zhou Zhongyue, Lu Han, Zhang Banghan, Xu Jizu, Zhu Xu, Li Peiyan, Lu Hexiang, Zhou Zongshun, He Yao, Chen Yuke, etc. as standing committee members, and have approved and implemented the donation methods. The method is based on the goal of raising enough funds for seventy airplanes, with each airplane temporarily set at 150,000 yuan. The provincial capital will raise funds for fourteen airplanes, the outer counties and administrative regions will raise funds for thirty-eight airplanes, national salvation lottery tickets will be issued for fourteen airplanes, and other sources will raise funds for four airplanes. The raised airplanes will be used for commercial purposes in peacetime and will be available for military use in wartime. When raising funds, assets will be used as the standard, divided into six levels: (A) Assets of 100,000 yuan or more in cash will donate 15%; (B) 50,000 yuan or more but less than 100,000 yuan will donate 10%; (C) 30,000 yuan or more but less than 50,000 yuan will donate 8%; (D) 10,000 yuan or more but less than 30,000 yuan will donate 4%; (E) 5,000 yuan or more but less than 10,000 yuan will donate 2%; (F) 1,000 yuan or more but less than 5,000 yuan will donate 1%. However, as the matter is of great importance, the association has specially entrusted Ma Chunlong, a member of the Chamber of Commerce, to take advantage of his investigation of industry and commerce to promote and solicit donations together. After Mr. Ma arrived in Shanghai, he has consulted with the responsible officers of the Yunnan Fellow Provincials Association in Shanghai several times. It has been agreed that everyone has a responsibility for the great plan of saving the country, and there are still many Yunnan people in Shanghai. A meeting of fellow provincials is planned to be convened within days to discuss all the donation methods, so as to advance together both internally and externally and accomplish the great plan together.

Road Construction Beyond Boundaries

Telephone Case Has Been Negotiated

Reporting Fees Passed on to Users

The Great American Evening News reported that the telephone contract for road construction beyond boundaries has been delayed in signing because the issue of how to handle the fees required to be reported to the municipal government and the Shanghai Telephone Bureau has not been resolved. It is now heard that this project has been negotiated and agreed upon. The total cost of the fees to be reported in a year is approximately 27,000 taels. Of this amount, nearly half is to be reported to the Shanghai Telephone Bureau. The Shanghai Telephone Company will temporarily treat this amount as a deferred debt, which will be calculated when telephone fees are revised in the future, that is, it will indirectly be borne by all users. The remaining amount to be reported to the Shanghai Municipal Government will be borne half by the telephone users in the roads constructed beyond boundaries and half by the users in the western district, northern district, Zhabei, southern city, and Pudong. As to how the users will bear these fees, nothing is yet known, but it is said that the increase in fees for the users in the western district, northern district, Zhabei, southern city, and Pudong will be extremely small.

China-British Boxer Indemnity Fund

Approving the Railroad Department's Proposal to Borrow Funds First

Approximately Over One Million Pounds Recommended for Allocation at the Next Board Meeting

Shanghai Times Electric News Agency reports that the Finance Committee of the Board of Directors of the China-British Boxer Indemnity Fund held its 24th meeting yesterday afternoon at the Bank Club. Those in attendance included Zeng Rongpu, Massey, Song Ziliang, Ye Gongchuo, and Tanner. Those attending as observers included Chen Yaozu, Director of the Railroad Department, and Hang Liwu, the General Secretary of the fund. The item for discussion was the Railroad Department's request to borrow funds first to complete the Guangdong-Hankou Railway, etc. The resolution was to recommend to the Board of Directors meeting next Monday to approve the department's borrowing of existing funds and subsequent funds that become due, approximately over one million pounds. However, the list of materials must be reviewed by the Technical Committee, and all previous collateral, such as passenger and freight rate increases, revenue from the capital ferry, revenue from the Guangzhou-Shaoguan section, and surpluses from the Pinghan Railway, must be clearly listed in the contract. It is also heard that the fund is scheduled to hold its 15th Board of Directors meeting next Monday in Nanjing. In addition to deciding on the loan of materials for the Guangdong-Hankou Railway, there will also be major cases to be discussed, such as the Ministry of Industry's request to borrow materials to jointly operate a distillery with Shanghai merchants, and the Construction Committee's request to allocate 100,000 yuan in cash to reorganize the capital power plant's lines, etc.

Baoshan Public Telephone Communication

Can Connect to Each Bureau Along the Shanghai City and Special District Routes

Since the Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications restored the Wusong telephone, it has set up a public telephone in Baoshan City, which can communicate with the Shanghai City, Concession Special District, and each bureau along the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou routes. However, as Baoshan City is not within the scope of Shanghai City, the communication procedures are slightly different from ordinary users. The methods are as follows: (1) All users who have deposited rent for Chinese and foreign calls or long-distance calls can communicate with Baoshan. (2) All users who call the Baoshan telephone (Wusong No. 11) should call out "Baoshan" (or directly call "Wusong No. 11") so that the dispatcher at the originating bureau can record it. (3) After a user communicates with Baoshan (that is, Wusong No. 11), whether the listener is the person called or not, the fees must be paid according to the regulations. (4) If a user calls the Baoshan telephone (that is, Wusong No. 11) and needs to summon the listener, in addition to providing the listener's name and address in detail, the telephone should be hung up immediately to indicate that the call is over and wait for a return call. If the telephone is not hung up or is shaken off, the waiting time will also be charged. (5) All telephones called out from the Baoshan public telephone (that is, Wusong No. 11) must be recorded by the Wusong dispatcher for charging purposes, regardless of whether they are return calls or requests for numbers. (6) If a telephone is called out from the Wusong public telephone (that is, Wusong No. 11) and is a return call, but the original caller at the other bureau has left impatiently, the telephone fee must still be paid. (7) The prescribed communication fees for the Baoshan public telephone (that is, Wusong No. 11) are 5 cents to Wusong, 8 cents to Nanshi and Zhabei, and 10 cents to the Concession. The same fees apply when calling from Wusong, etc., to Baoshan City. If long-distance calls to Beijing-Shanghai or Shanghai-Hangzhou are made, the fees should be added according to the regulations.

Returning Savings from the Three Northeastern Provinces

Registration Has Begun

Bureau of Savings and Remittances Announces Repayment Measures

After the General Bureau of Postal Savings and Remittances, with the approval of the Ministry of Finance, ordered the repayment of savings in the three northeastern provinces, Mr. Fang Tinghua, the head of the Savings Department of the bureau, drafted the repayment regulations and registration procedures. The bureau notified the postal administrations in each district yesterday and simultaneously announced the repayment regulations and began registration. The details are as follows:

Postal Notice: This is to announce that all depositors within the three northeastern provinces who hold savings deposit books or fixed deposit certificates issued by the Liaoning postal district before July 23, 1932, and by the Jilin and Heilongjiang postal districts before July 25, 1932, must register in person or through their agents at the bureau. This notice is hereby issued so that everyone may be informed.

Repayment Regulations: (1) Savings deposit books can be registered at any post office (excluding sub-branches) within the country that handles savings deposits. Fixed deposit certificates can be registered at post offices (excluding sub-branches) that handle fixed deposits. (2) If depositors wish to keep their savings in the post office, after one month from the date of registration, the registering post office will exchange the old book or certificate for a new one. Savings deposit books and certificates in the Jilin and Heilongjiang districts that were deposited in Haikou silver and do not specify silver dollars will be converted into silver dollars at 80% of their face value. Interest on these retained savings will accrue from the day after the last interest settlement date of the northeastern post offices (i.e., from July 1, 1932). Interest on fixed deposits will be calculated from the original deposit date at the original interest rate. (3) If depositors wish to withdraw these savings, they must also wait one month from the date of registration and then, as usual, submit a withdrawal slip, along with the savings book or fixed deposit certificate, to the original registering office to withdraw the savings. All withdrawal slips and fixed deposit certificates must be signed and stamped with the original seal of the depositor. The interest on the total savings withdrawn will be calculated according to the method in section two above, up to the date of registration. (4) If deemed necessary, the post office may ask the depositor to provide a guarantor with a solid business reputation before repaying the savings. (5) All matters related to the repayment of savings will be handled at the original registering office. If the original savings were deposited in Haikou silver (see section two above), they will be repaid in silver dollars converted at 80% of their face value.

Scope of Registration: According to Mr. Fang Tinghua, the head of the Savings Department, all registration forms and other items have been printed with designs and distributed to various postal administrations for printing so that depositors can obtain and fill them out. To facilitate registration for depositors, registration can be done in Tianjin, Beiping, Hankou, Qingdao, Shanghai, Guangdong, and other postal districts that handle postal remittances. The total amount to be repaid this time is approximately 230,000 yuan.

Antiquities from the Academia Sinica

Will Be Exhibited in Shanghai

丨Arrangements to be Made Once the Third Batch Arrives丨

After the decision was made to move the Institute of History and Philology and the Institute of Psychology of the Academia Sinica in Beiping south, in addition to the 120 boxes of antiquities previously transported to Shanghai, there were still 400 boxes. It was originally planned to transport them to Shanghai with the second batch of antiquities from the Palace Museum, but since they were not loaded, they will be transported to Shanghai with the third batch of antiquities from the Palace Museum. According to Mr. Yang Xingfo, after all the antiquities are loaded and transported to Shanghai, they will be displayed in the new building of the Academia Sinica on Avenue Henri Bazin for exhibition.

Vietnamese Constable's Murder Case

French Consul-General Replies to the Municipal Government

The French Municipal Council Provides 2,000 Yuan Each for the Families of the Deceased

According to the Central News Agency, regarding the case of a Vietnamese constable shooting and killing a Chinese person in the French Concession, the Support Association for the case previously petitioned the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate with the French Consulate. However, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs stated that the case was a local matter and should be handled by the local government. In addition to instructing the association, it also sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Government for investigation and handling, as previously reported. It is now learned that the French Consulate-General has sent a reply to the Municipal Government, which is excerpted below: In reply to your letter No. 172 of the 13th of this month, received with respect. The following facts are hereby reported: On February 25th, a Vietnamese constable was escorting a person who had violated police regulations on Rue du Pont Neuf to the police station when a large number of passers-by suddenly attacked, attempting to rescue the violator. During the struggle, the Vietnamese constable fired a shot with live ammunition, which accidentally went off, injuring passers-by and resulting in the death of two people. Afterward, a criminal investigation was immediately conducted on the Vietnamese constable, and the French Consular Court will try the case. Respect for the judiciary is required, so no comments can be made on the responsibility of the accused before the verdict of the court with jurisdiction. In order to urgently assist the families of the two deceased Chinese, the French Municipal Council has provided 2,000 yuan each for the families of the deceased, and the families have agreed to accept it. In response to the previous letter, the above is respectfully reported to your mayor for your information. With best wishes, 梅禮靄 (Mei Liai).

Workers at the Nanyang Tobacco Factory

Petitioned the Municipal Government Yesterday

The Bureau of Social Affairs is Scheduled to Mediate Again Today

A dispute has recently arisen at the Nanyang Tobacco Factory on Broadway Road in Hongkou due to workers' demands for improved treatment. The workers petitioned the Municipal Government yesterday, and the Bureau of Social Affairs convened a mediation session. The Special District Court opened a trial yesterday. The details are as follows:

Petition to the Municipal Government: Workers' representatives Zhang Zhang, Weng Lin, Xu Zhubao, Yu Xingqing, and Wang Jiansheng, carrying a written petition, went to the Municipal Government yesterday afternoon. Since Mayor Wu was out, Zhang Chengwu of the Municipal Government received them. The representatives put forward five demands: (1) Release the arrested workers. (2) Order the factory to withdraw all security vehicles and Chinese and foreign detectives. (3) Order the Bureau of Social Affairs to resolve the preliminary conditions for labor and management as soon as possible. (4) Send a letter to the First Special District Court to notify the police not to arbitrarily arrest workers. (5) Stop the arrest warrants for union leaders. Mr. Zhang expressed acceptance and promised to forward the matter to the mayor for review. The workers' representatives were satisfied and left.

Petition to the Municipal Government: The union's petition to the Municipal Government states: Regarding the Nanyang Tobacco Factory, which experienced a decline in business and capital losses in 1929, leading to a temporary shutdown, all employees, aware of the situation and unwilling to see a Chinese industrial factory fail, adopted the principle of labor-management cooperation to jointly develop the industry. They voluntarily reduced wages, increased work, endured hardships, and worked hard to produce, cooperating sincerely with the factory. As a result, business gradually improved in recent years, with a profit of over one million yuan throughout 1932. While the employees do not dare to claim credit for this, they can take comfort in it. However, the factory management not only disregarded the employees' hard work in supporting the factory and showed no compassion but also wantonly trampled on and heavily oppressed them, causing labor-management relations to deteriorate and the previous spirit of cooperation to disintegrate. (omitted) Therefore, at 10:00 AM on the 20th of this month, they all spontaneously went on strike to express their determination and urge the factory to realize the situation. After party and government authorities sent personnel to the factory to mediate and persuade them to resume work, a dispute arose. Representative Zhang Decheng was arrested by the police and transferred to the court. In the past two days, responsible representatives Wu Shiyuan, Li Ajin, and Li Gui were successively arrested and also transferred to the court, but have not been released. The factory is using all kinds of despicable and insidious means to destroy the workers' organization, which shows its intentions. The union, having the important responsibility of representing the entire factory's workers, should be given reasonable protection. In addition to petitioning the city party headquarters and the Bureau of Social Affairs for review, representatives Zhang Zhang and others have been sent to present the situation and petition. We implore your government to review and approve the matter and order the Bureau of Social Affairs to promptly convene labor and management for mediation on the preliminary conditions for labor and management. We also request that the Nanyang Tobacco Factory be ordered to stop arresting worker representatives, and that the arrested worker representatives be released to benefit the labor movement. The undersigned is eager to await your command. Respectfully submitted by Zhou Xuexiang, Standing Committee Member of the Fourth District Cigarette Industry Union, to Mayor Wu.

Convening Mediation: In order to prevent the expansion of the dispute, the Bureau of Social Affairs convened a mediation session between labor and management at 2:00 PM yesterday. The Nanyang factory sent its legal advisor, Wu Linkun, as its representative, and the labor side was represented by Zhang Zhang. The mediation was chaired by Wang Xianqing, Director of the Mediation Section of the Bureau of Social Affairs. As the management did not attend in person, no mediation could be conducted. It was rescheduled for 10:00 AM tomorrow (the 25th) at the Bureau of Social Affairs, with a strict order that the factory send an important official to attend.

Court Opens Trial: The case of Zhang Desheng, foreman of the tobacco leaf section of the Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company, assaulting employee Li Zhitang and others has been transferred by the Hongkou Huishan police to the First Special District Court, charging Zhang and his followers Wu Shiyuan and Li Ajin with crimes such as assault and destruction of property. Under questioning by the judge, they were ordered to be detained pending investigation. The police also arrested Li Gui, a worker in the tobacco leaf section, and Li Xinfang, a carpenter, the day before yesterday. Yesterday morning, witnesses Feng Haiquan, Wang Huifa, He Ganyun, Chen Fengxiang, and Zhu Yonghua were summoned and sent to the First Special District Court. Judge Xiao Xiexun conducted the interrogation. Zhang Tianyin, the police lawyer, presented the circumstances of the recent disturbance. He then stated that Zhang Desheng and others had been scheduled for a hearing on the 28th and requested that this case also be rescheduled to be heard together. Then, witnesses such as Feng Haiquan testified that Li Gui wielded an iron rod at the scene to assault people, and Li Xinfang, although unarmed, was also supporting the assault at the scene. Wu Linkun, the representative lawyer of the Nanyang Company, appeared in court as an observer. After the court briefly questioned the defendants, it ordered them to be detained pending rescheduling for a joint hearing.

Union Office: The Nanyang Tobacco Factory Office of the Fourth District Cigarette Industry Union was formally established on the 12th. Due to the current dispute, the union's affairs have been disrupted. To facilitate contact with all parties, the office has temporarily been located at 106 Qiaojia Road in the Nanshi area. The office issued a statement and a letter to workers yesterday, which were very tactful and moving, and are therefore omitted.

Japanese Envoy Arima Returns to Japan Today

Talks with Japanese Journalists Yesterday

The Japanese Shanghai Daily News reports that the Japanese Envoy to China, Arima Akira, is scheduled to return to Japan today at 9:00 AM, accompanied by Secretary Okazaki and Secretary Asaka, on the Nagasaki Maru. Yesterday, he met with a group of journalists (from Japanese newspapers) and made the following remarks: I (Arima refers to himself) plan to stay in Japan for about three weeks. After arriving in Tokyo on the morning of the 27th, I will immediately meet with Foreign Minister Uchida and then go to Kyoto on the 2nd of next month. Rumors that I am returning to Japan to make important suggestions are completely untrue. There is always telegraphic communication between Shanghai and Tokyo to convey ideas. When I met with Jiang Zuobin the other day, we only talked about interesting things such as hot springs and forests, and did not mention any major issues.

Chinese Ratepayers Association

Sets Date for Municipal Elections

Ballots Have Been Issued Yesterday

Ballot Counting to Begin on the 27th

The 12th Shanghai International Settlement Chinese Ratepayers Association election is scheduled for March 27th. Ballots were checked yesterday by representatives of various groups, totaling 4,465 votes without error. They were then delivered to the post office under supervision at 2:00 PM and mailed to each voter. The letters to each voter and each group are recorded below:

To Each Voter: Dear Sir/Madam, The 12th election of the Association has been announced in the newspaper with the qualifications of voters and candidates determined. The voting period is set from 9:00 AM to 5:00 PM on March 27th. The ballot box will be located at the Bankers' Association hall downstairs in the Association's building. Ballot counting will begin at 9:00 AM the following morning. Enclosed are a ballot paper, a list of candidates, and an admission ticket. Please refer to the election instructions printed on the ballot paper. As this concerns the exercise of your right to vote, please do not abandon it. With best wishes.

To Each Group: Dear Sir/Madam, The 12th election of our Association has been scheduled. Election ballots will be sent out at 1:00 PM on March 23rd. You are hereby requested to send a representative to our Association at that time to check the number of ballots and send them to the post office in a solemn manner. We hope you will take note of this.

News on Foreign Ratepayers' Elections

The Shanghai Evening Post reports that the British Ratepayers Association Committee has considered the issue of the Municipal Council elections and agreed that, in order to avoid an unequal representation of foreign taxpayers, two Japanese candidates and two American candidates should be elected. As for the British candidates, they felt it unnecessary to offer any suggestions and would leave it to the voters to elect them as they wished.

The election dates are next Monday and Tuesday, with two polling locations: one at the Municipal Council building at 209 Jiangxi Road and one at the Hongkou Police Station, from 10:00 AM to 3:00 PM.

Municipal Council Candidates' Political Views

Recording Shortcomings of the Court

Curbing Anti-Japanese Boycotts

Opposing Increased Number of Chinese Councilors

Inspecting Factories

The British candidates for the Shanghai Municipal Council, Peel and six others, published their political views in the Shanghai Western newspapers yesterday:

Peel said, "If re-elected, I intend to continue my previous policy of striving to maintain the rights and freedoms of the International Settlement and cooperate with the authorities in the neighboring areas to seek common welfare. In particular, I intend to seek a satisfactory agreement regarding the roads built outside the Settlement. I advocate strict reductions in government spending, but I will not be stingy with the funds used to maintain the peace and reputation of the Settlement."

Blair said, "If elected, I intend to support policies that move towards the greatest possible municipal cooperation, in order to maintain the interests of the Settlement according to the broadest possible interpretation."

Arnold said, "If re-elected, I intend to continue the policies implemented by the Municipal Council last year and will not allow the rights of the International Settlement to be eroded. The Municipal Council has two major issues that deserve attention: (1) Closely scrutinizing all expenses, because based on current spending, it will soon be necessary to increase tax rates or raise huge debts. (2) Concluding an agreement with the Shanghai Municipal Government regarding the construction of roads outside the Settlement. Currently, public utilities such as the electricity company, water company, and telephone company cannot connect with new users until this agreement is reached. The prolonged unresolved issue of roads outside the Settlement is a major obstacle to concluding such contracts."

Massey said, "If re-elected, I will do my best to mediate the unfortunate dispute between the landlords and the water company, maintain the strength of the defense forces and police, and, to the extent that finances allow, promote beneficial sanitation and general development projects. I will especially focus on improving the administration of the District Court."

Harris said, "I believe that the most important thing now is to maintain the integrity and security of the foreign settlements. The peace, tranquility, and prosperity of Shanghai and the surrounding areas should be given first consideration. When we are surrounded by this state of disturbance, we cannot show any weakness in upholding our treaty rights. The District Court agreement has now been extended for another three years. This issue will not be raised for consideration this year, but the Municipal Council should carefully monitor the administration of the court. Any inappropriate judgments or executions should be recorded one by one, so that when the agreement is revised in the future, evidence of the current organizational and operational shortcomings of the court can be presented, and a judicial system that can guarantee fairness for all can be demanded. One of the most important issues awaiting resolution today is the status of roads outside the Settlement. I believe that while maintaining the essential elements of effective police management, an agreement can be reached with the Chinese authorities that allows for legitimate and necessary expansion and allows those who currently reside or will reside in the expanded area to live in peace and receive the benefits of various public utilities necessary for life. As for the important issue of Shanghai's future status, it seems that it will soon be considered by the major powers. I believe that the foreign residents of Shanghai should unite to form a foreign association that can serve as a platform for expressing their opinions. All matters involving the interests of Shanghai should be discussed with the Shanghai Municipal Council and the French Municipal Council, and they should be allowed to have appropriate representation. This is extremely important. The Municipal Council's first responsibility is to focus on the best interests of the residents in governing the Settlement, maintaining peace and order, and curbing illegal activities and anti-Japanese boycotts. If the Municipal Council's power to act is insufficient, it should use various opportunities to make this power appropriately sufficient. I have conducted special research in finance and economics for the past 25 years, so I believe that we should be aware of the impact of the economic downturn on cities around the world and prepare for possible methods to prevent this trend from affecting Shanghai."

Macnaghten said, "If elected, I will do my best to maintain the esteemed integrity of the Settlement's administration. Regarding the Municipal Council's policies and the allocation of government funds, the safety and sanitation of the citizens should be given first consideration. In terms of safety, I will never be stingy with the expenses of maintaining the effectiveness of the police, fire department, and merchant corps. Although Shanghai is temporarily peaceful on the surface, past history tells us that disturbances often come like a sudden hurricane, with little prior warning. Therefore, we must always be prepared to deal with emergencies. In terms of sanitation, I will also never be stingy with the funds for purchasing open spaces and public works. I also believe that when a special meeting of taxpayers is convened in the future to discuss revising the bylaws and limiting the licensing of factories, a sufficient number of people will be able to attend to meet the statutory quorum. I firmly believe that Shanghai has a boundless future and recognize that traffic problems are also extremely important. My traffic policy advocates three things: developing transportation facilities between the city and outlying areas, quickly resolving the issue of roads outside the Settlement, and expanding the scope of activities of existing public utility companies to provide public utility services to gradually prosperous areas outside the Settlement."

Landale said, "My approach and views on municipal administration are roughly as follows: As China continues to be turbulent and unstable, we should strive to protect the rights of foreign taxpayers in the Settlement as permitted by the Yangjingbang Regulations. Without increasing the number of foreign directors, we oppose further increasing the number of Chinese directors. We should try to resolve the issue of roads outside the Settlement as soon as possible. We should also rely on the full strength of the police, supplemented by incentives for volunteer service and special constables, to do our best to ensure the peace and security of the Settlement, because the troops stationed in Shanghai from various countries may be withdrawn at any time. Because the duties of the police are extremely important and dangerous, they must not be left with vacancies. I also believe that the time has come for the Municipal Council to manage factories and should give the Municipal Council the power to issue licenses and inspect factories. Regarding education and the problems of Chinese people in the Settlement, due to the Municipal Council's limited finances, the matter must be carefully considered. It is believed that education funding should be limited to a certain percentage of the Settlement's total income. Subsidies for various agencies that handle work beneficial to the public should also be given sympathetic consideration. I certainly know that if the above are implemented, it will inevitably increase expenditures, but if this money can be used properly, it may prove to be an economic move in the long run. Even if the cost of living is rising daily, a slight increase in taxes may not be very objectionable. In addition, the election method in the Yangjingbang Regulations should also be revised."

Railway Department Suspends Station Relocation

Pengpu Municipal Committee Requests Resumption of Sales

The Ministry of Railways used civilian land in the Pengpu Zhenru area to relocate the Shanghai North Railway Station on the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo railways. Now, the Ministry of Railways has temporarily suspended the relocation due to the current national crisis. The Pengpu Municipal Committee, Zhou Bulian and Ling Zhibin, stated that tens of thousands of acres of land in Pengpu have been suspended from sale, affecting tens of thousands of farming households. Since the Ministry of Railways is not buying the land, it should be released for sale immediately to relieve the local economy and benefit the people's livelihood. They have submitted this intention to the Municipal Government.

Military Affairs Commission

Shanghai Office Receives Relief Goods

Already Handed Over to the Railway Bureau to Transport to the Front Lines Free of Charge

According to the Central News Agency, the Shanghai Office of the General Affairs Department of the Military Affairs Commission received relief goods yesterday from the Chinese Women's Relief Association for Compatriots in the Northeast, including 3,000 pairs of rubber shoes, 50,000 cigarettes, four bolts and 32 packages of gauze, 1,100 sets of sanitary clothing, 1,000 sets of military uniforms, 1,000 sets of civilian clothing, 1,045 pairs of goggles, 60 vests, 6,000 pairs of socks, 2,000 yards of twill fabric, and 2,100 towels. The office sent personnel to check and seal them before handing them over to the Railway Bureau to transport them to the front lines free of charge to comfort the loyal and brave soldiers defending the country.

Ministry of Finance Approves Export of Silver Coins

Issued an Order Yesterday to the Jianghai Customs to Comply

The Ministry of Finance has issued an order to the Jianghai Customs in Shanghai regarding the export of legal silver coins, with passports issued by the supervisory authority: Regarding the implementation of measures to ban the transportation of silver coins, since the implementation of the regulations, if legal silver coins are transported from foreign ports to domestic ports and there is a certificate from the foreign Chinese Chamber of Commerce, they should be temporarily allowed to be imported. The currency department of the Shanghai Customs Department had previously agreed with the currency department to stipulate that the customs department should order the Inspector General of Customs to comply. Now it has been stipulated that legal silver coins transported from domestic ports to foreign ports will be allowed to be exported with a passport issued by the supervisory authority to facilitate circulation. The remaining provisions will still be handled in accordance with the previous ban on transportation measures. In addition to issuing separate orders, the superintendent is hereby ordered to comply with this order and instruct the Customs Commissioner to comply with it.

Losing all conscience and reason

Enduring to Sell Large Quantities of Old Iron to Aid the Enemy

Remote Yangjing Town in Pudong

Has Recently Made Two Transactions

It has recently come to our attention that Japanese agents are buying up large quantities of old iron in China. This has occurred several times in Shanghai alone. Unexpectedly, someone has even been purchasing iron in the remote town of Yangjing in Pudong. There have been two transactions recently. The enthusiastic residents nearby all believe that the sellers are greedy for profit and are heartlessly aiding the enemy. They are all extremely indignant. The following is a record of the information we have been able to gather. However, the actions of both the buyer and seller are kept strictly secret, making it very difficult to obtain full details.

First Time, 100 Loads: The first transaction took place on the 13th of this month. A certain sugar mill in the town loaded over 100 loads of old iron onto a ship at 4:00 PM, preparing to transport it out. It is said that a Japanese person had arrived at the mill one day prior to negotiate, agreeing on a price of 280 taels of silver, which was paid in full at the time. This was discovered by a Mr. Pan, a citizen of the town, who witnessed several people carrying the iron onto the ship. He was overcome with anger and reported it to a certain authority, requesting that it be seized. It is unknown how it was handled at the time.

Second Time, 500 Loads: The second transaction took place on the 20th of this month. A certain sugar mill in Xizhakou, also in the town, carried over 500 loads of old iron that had been gradually accumulated, to the Yangjing port at 2:00 PM, loading it onto two large ships. Just as they were about to cast off, a certain detective happened to see it and immediately reported it to a certain authority for a decision. The outcome is unknown.

Heavy Rain in the City Yesterday

Midday Sky Suddenly Darkens

The weather in the city has been erratic lately, alternating between cold and warm. Yesterday morning around 9:00 AM, it started with a light drizzle, followed by a dense cloud cover. It looked like a downpour was imminent. By 1:00 PM, it had become exceptionally dark. Stores along the roads turned on their electric lights to do business. A heavy rain soon followed, accompanied by thunder. The dark clouds dispersed after about an hour, but the rain continued to fall.

City Bank Moves into New Premises

The Shanghai City Bank has been in operation for three years since its establishment. Its business has been thriving year after year, with great momentum. Due to the increase in capital and expansion of business, the original bank premises were no longer sufficient. They have selected the old site at No. 24 Tianjin Road, opposite the original location, as the new bank premises. The renovations have been completed in recent days. It is said that they are scheduled to move into the new premises on the 27th of this month, and refreshments will be provided to welcome guests from all walks of life to visit and provide guidance. It is expected that there will be a grand occasion at that time.

Lawyers Association to Hold a General Meeting

The Shanghai Lawyers Association has scheduled a spring general meeting for all members on April 16th (Sunday) at the Lake Society on Beijing Road in the Public Concession. The executive and supervisory committee members will be re-elected. In addition to having requested the Shanghai District Court and the First and Second Special District District Courts to send prosecutors to supervise the meeting, the City Party Department has also been invited to send personnel to attend and provide guidance. A notice has been sent to all members, stating: Respectfully, we hereby announce that the spring regular general meeting will be held at 2:00 PM on April 16th (Sunday) this year at the Lake Society on Beijing Road, and officers will be re-elected. Any member who has a proposal should submit it to the association ten days before the meeting so that it can be printed and distributed. Additional Canal Tax and Exemption from Late Payment Penalties

The Finance Bureau of the Shanghai County government issued a public notice yesterday, stating that it had received an instruction from the Jiangsu Finance Department, which stated that the Qingpu, Songjiang, and other counties had successively telegraphed, stating that the people were feeling the burden of the two yuan additional canal tax, which was continued for another year. They were painfully paying the increased tax. Moreover, after the disasters of war and floods, the local vitality had not yet recovered. Furthermore, the low price of grain was harming farmers, and the economy was becoming even more depleted. They requested that the late payment penalties for the additional canal tax be waived to alleviate the people's hardship. All late payment penalties for the additional canal tax should be approved and exempted from calculation, and a uniform order should be issued. In addition to issuing instructions to other departments, the director of the bureau should be instructed to comply accordingly. In accordance with this order, the late payment penalties for the two yuan additional canal tax under the second installment of the twenty-first year land price tax are reduced and exempted from collection. In addition to instructing the grain counter to comply, a public notice is issued to all households in the county for their information.

Permit Regulations Specify 17,000 Vehicles

Dispute Resolved at the Siyi Silk Factory

The Siyi Silk Factory on Zhoujiazui Road in Hongkou, specializing in weaving Chinese silk georgette and Indian silk, has more than 60 male and female workers. The original wages were 9 and a half cents per yard for Chinese silk georgette and 6 cents per yard for Indian silk. Recently, the management wanted to reduce the wages by 20%, which was opposed by all the workers. The management closed the factory gate on the morning of the 21st of this month, refusing to let the workers work, causing a dispute. The workers immediately petitioned the Social Bureau, requesting it to intervene. Yesterday at 3:00 PM, the Social Bureau summoned both labor and management for mediation. Chen Biheng and Yu Shuli represented the labor side, and Zhang Zhongyu and Zhang Jilu represented the management side. The mediation was chaired by Tan Peiyan of the Social Bureau. The results of the mediation were: (1) The factory will be responsible for continuing to operate at the end of April. (2) The workers will return to their hometowns, and the factory will provide them with travel expenses of 8 yuan. (3) If the factory cannot be opened by the deadline, in addition to being legally dismissed, they will be given a subsidy of 10 yuan for meals. At that time, both labor and management were satisfied, and the mediation was concluded.

泰德芝 (Tai De Zhi - likely a foreign name)

Repeat Offender of Opium Trafficking

Imprisonment for a Year and a Half and a Fine of 3,000 Yuan

Qin Dezhi, a native of Wuxi, was found some time ago with a package of raw opium weighing two pounds hidden on his person. He was passing through the intersection of Zhengjia Muqiao Street on Avenue Edward VII when he was spotted by detectives, who found his actions suspicious. They searched him and found the raw opium, and brought him to the police station. It was found that Qin had previously been convicted of transporting opium and had been punished by the court. The chief ordered him to be detained and sent to the Second Special District Court, where he was publicly prosecuted under Article 6 of the Anti-Opium Law. According to Qin's confession, he was sending it to the North Station to be handed over to a Mr. Wang to be taken to another city. After a trial, Judge Wu Fanglian yesterday sentenced the defendant to one year and six months of imprisonment and a fine of 3,000 yuan for repeatedly possessing raw opium with the intention of trafficking. The raw opium was confiscated.

Cook in Congee Shop Suddenly Slashed

Two Assailants Fled the Scene

Zhao Jintong, a 27-year-old man from Danyang, was working as a cook at the Zhan Xingjiang Congee Shop at No. 52 on Baoliqiao Road in the French Concession. At around 6:00 AM today, while Zhao was working in the shop, two people suddenly rushed into the shop with kitchen knives. Without asking any questions, they slashed Zhao three times, once in the back and once on each hand. Zhao cried out for help and immediately fell to the ground, seriously injured. The assailants, seeing that their goal had been achieved, fled the scene. The shop owner later transported him to Renji Hospital for treatment.

Two Cases of Assault with Sharp Weapons

Suspicion Arises: Zheng A'wu, a man from Ningbo residing at No. 47 Renchang Lane, Qiwu Pu Road, Yangshupu, is 29 years old and works as a sampan rower for the water patrol. Shallow Water Fees for the Xiang River Completely Abolished

Effective Today

Last winter, due to the receding water levels in the Xiang River, transportation was inconvenient. The various shipping companies decided to increase the shallow water fees, by as much as eighty percent. Since the beginning of spring, the water level in that route has gradually risen. On the first of this month, the shallow water fees were reduced by thirty percent, leaving a remaining fifty percent. Yesterday, the various companies in this port received a telegram from their Hankou branch, stating that the remaining fifty percent of the shallow water fees has now been decided to be completely abolished starting tomorrow (i.e., today), the fourteenth. After receiving the telegram, the companies immediately notified the customs brokers to inform their clients. However, the shallow water fees for the Hankou to Yichang and Shashi route will remain temporarily unchanged, but it is expected that they will also be abolished soon.

Bodyguard's Shout of Kidnapping

Actually Scares Away the Kidnappers

Zhang Yunjin Escapes Kidnappers' Grasp

Kidnappers' Elaborate Prearrangements

Some Selling Wonton, Some Pulling Rickshaws

Fleeing in Panic at the Shout, Abandoning Handgun

The Kidnapping of Zhou Xitang Also By Such Ruffians

Zhang Yunjin, a native of Ningbo, 50 years old, lives at No. 359 Gaoun Road in the French Concession. He runs a hardware store in Fengtian and is in modest circumstances, owning a private car with license plate number 6577, driven by Xue Sichuan, a local resident. Because kidnapping cases are rampant nowadays, for protection, he hired Qiu Zhaoshan from Hebei as a bodyguard, who accompanies him everywhere. Zhang is fond of Peking opera and regularly goes to the Zhengyi Theater at No. 184 Shandong Road, Nanjing Road, to learn Peking opera. Before 2:00 AM yesterday morning (i.e., late at night on the 22nd), Zhang, his wife, and Qiu Zhaoshan went to Zhengyi Theater again. At 2:15 AM, as they exited the theater, suddenly six or seven kidnappers, each holding a handgun, stepped forward and threatened Zhang, intending to kidnap him. At that time, Qiu Zhaoshan, unprepared, did not have time to resist with his gun and had no choice but to shout "Kidnapping!" The kidnappers, hearing the shout, were greatly alarmed and feared that the police would arrive. They abandoned Zhang and fled in all directions. The responsible general police station received a report and immediately ordered Chinese detectives Xie Shuiquan, Pang Ruiqing, Geng Debiao, and others to rush to the scene to search for the kidnappers. However, the kidnappers had already disappeared without a trace. After investigation by Detective Xie and others, it was learned that the kidnappers' procedures this time were quite thorough. They had all disguised themselves beforehand, some as wonton sellers, others as rickshaw pullers, and lay in wait in the small alley next to the Zhengyi Theater to avoid the attention of police officers. The kidnappers' failure this time was all due to Qiu Zhaoshan's shout. In their hasty escape, the kidnappers even left behind a handgun with nine bullets at the corner of Nanjing Road and Henan Road, in front of the Hengdali Watch Shop. The detectives picked it up and found that the gun's number was 443803. The gun belonged to Zhou Xitang, a comprador of the Lao Gongmao Foreign Firm, whose bodyguard, a Russian named Wei Weisha Luofu, was carrying it. Recently, Zhou was suddenly attacked by a number of kidnappers near the Dada Wharf in the Chinese territory. Zhou resisted, and the kidnappers opened fire, wounding Zhou and killing the bodyguard Wei on the spot, stealing the gun Wei was carrying and scattering. Zhou also died of his injuries at Tongren Hospital. From this, it can be inferred that the kidnappers who kidnapped Zhang were the same ones who killed Zhou and Wei. The detectives later found two carrying poles left behind by the kidnappers next to the Zhengyi Theater. Along with the handgun, they were taken back to the police station and reported to the police chief, who informed all police stations to jointly arrest the escaped kidnappers.

Five Robbers Escape by Jumping Over Roofs

Wounded Robber Seeks Treatment at Hospital, Gets Arrested

Wounded Robber Falsely Claims to Be Rickshaw Puller Hit by Stray Bullet

But How Can Rickshaw Puller Wear Woolen Pants and Woolen Socks?

Two People Accompanying Him to Hospital Also Confess to Being Robbers

At 7:10 PM last night, five robbers suddenly came to the home of Zhang Zhenbang, a Ningbo native who runs a leather goods business at No. 3, Fuzhi Lane, No. 344 Beile Road in the French Concession. Three robbers, holding guns, entered the house and first confined everyone inside to the back living room. One robber stood guard with a gun, while the other four went upstairs to search and rob, stealing clothing and silver dollars worth about three hundred yuan. Just as they were about to escape through the door, someone had already secretly reported to the Songshan Road police station. The police chief immediately dispatched two French deputies, along with several detectives, to rush to the scene to arrest them. At that time, the French deputy first entered No. 4 next door. The French deputy turned the doorknob and was peeking into No. 3 when, unexpectedly, the robber on watch heard the police and immediately shouted to the four robbers upstairs to quickly come downstairs. At the same time, he watched the side door. Sure enough, someone opened the door, and he fired a shot at it, hitting the doorpost. The French deputy was shocked and closed the door again. The five robbers knew that there must be people lying in ambush at the front and back doors, so they rushed straight upstairs and fired a shot at the top of the staircase as a warning. When they reached the vicinity of the drying platform, they fired another shot and then jumped over the roofs together to escape. At that time, a Vietnamese constable at the back door saw the robbers jumping over the roofs and quickly aimed and fired a shot. As a result, all five robbers escaped like rabbits. However, at 9:15 PM, a man and a woman suddenly brought a young man with gunshot wounds to Renji Hospital for treatment, claiming that the injured person was a rickshaw puller named Liu Sanrong, 26 years old, from Funing, who had been hit by a stray bullet while pulling a rickshaw near the Great World. The rest of their words were evasive. Because it was a gunshot wound, the hospital, as a matter of routine, notified the police station by telephone. At the same time, the French police station, upon hearing the news, immediately dispatched detectives to investigate, and reporters accompanied them. It was found that the bullet had entered from the right rib and pierced through the back. The injured person was wearing a cotton short jacket, a black lined jacket, a gray cloth shirt, black checkered woolen pants, woolen socks, and rubber overshoes, but the lower part was completely free of mud, not at all like a rickshaw puller. After repeated questioning by the detectives, he continued to evade and deny. Upon closer inspection of the palm of his right hand, there was a fresh scratch mark covered with mud. The detectives concluded that he must be one of the robbers who committed the robbery at the scene, and the scratch on his palm was caused when he jumped over the roof. They then went downstairs and arrested the man and woman who brought him. At the same time, they telegraphed the police chief to order detectives to go to the hospital with the head of the victim's family, his wife, and his eldest son to identify the injured person as one of the five robbers at the scene. The arrested man and woman were taken to the police station. After strict interrogation, they also directly admitted to committing the robbery at the scene.

Reader's Advisor

Rural Bankruptcy and Unemployment Problems

丨Message from Mr. Wang Taixia of Lianshui丨

I am about to become a starving ghost. I beg you, sir, to point me to a bright way out. I will now describe my situation; I am a rickshaw puller, and there are three people in my family: a disabled father, a mother in her fifties, and myself. My family has more than three mu of land, which is usually cultivated by my mother alone; in my spare time from pulling the rickshaw, I also help her with the work. In recent years, there has been a drought, so these three mu of land are as good as nothing. In the past, I could earn more than one yuan a day pulling the rickshaw; now it is different, because the number of people pulling rickshaws is increasing every day, which has taken away a lot of my business. Now I can't even find a few cents a day; I am already heavily in debt. Now it is even worse, because two cars have been set up in my hometown; the rickshaw route that we usually rely on for a living has now been permanently taken away by them. Because they can carry a person for fifty or sixty li for only fifty cents, and they are fast, running three or four round trips a day. Our rickshaw business is directly gone, because we have to charge at least one yuan to carry a person for fifty or sixty li. We can only do one piece of business a day, and with business being bad now, we can't even rely on finding a piece of business in a few days. My family's life has reached the extreme of hardship, and the three of us can't even eat two meals of porridge a day. And it's not just my family, I'm afraid that most families who make a living by pulling rickshaws are like my family, right? Looking at their car station, money is like water every day, how happy is that?! I can't pull the rickshaw anymore, so I have to go to work as a long-term laborer for someone else; so I found two relatives to help me find a job as a long-term laborer for someone else. After a few days, my relatives came back and replied to me like this: there are no people in the countryside who need long-term laborers now, the servants of the wealthy families are already full, because people who have no land to cultivate due to the recent drought have all gone to work as long-term laborers for other people. Small households don't need people at all. Oh, enlightened sir? Are we just going to starve to death like this? We are almost starving to death now. I can't even find a messenger job in an office, because they are all full, and maybe there are people waiting! Alas! Where am I going? Where am I going to work for whom? What method am I going to use to support my two elderly parents? Knowledgeable reporter, please think of a perfect solution for me!

Answer: Your letter is truly worthy of our praise, because the facts you described reveal the true phenomenon of the current society, which is a picture of the intrusion of capitalism into the countryside, the rapid bankruptcy of the countryside, and the large-scale unemployment of farmers, not only farmers are unemployed, but also the cities cannot accommodate the large number of unemployed people from the countryside, thus becoming the unemployment of workers, etc. This phenomenon is of course universal, not just a problem for you alone, but a universal rural problem in China. If you want to solve your personal problems, you must start with solving the whole problem. In our opinion, to alleviate this panic, there should be at least the following ways: (1) Quickly stand on the side of the interests of the vast majority of farmers and solve the land problem in the countryside from a truly democratic point of view. (2) Those who have no land to cultivate, or who have land but are affected by disasters and have no way to make a living, or unemployed rural workers, should have an organization to gather together to study this problem. (3) With this organization, we can further study the physical causes of floods and droughts in the countryside, such as how to cultivate forests, how to improve agriculture, and at this time, everyone will realize that the so-called floods and droughts are not only due to nature, but in fact half of them are due to the results of a deformed and unequal social system. Therefore, to alleviate the panic in the countryside, we must first solve the farmers' land problem; to solve the land problem, farmers must first have their own organization; with an organization, they will naturally feel that the social system is closely related to the farmers. At that time, you will naturally see the way out ahead. You will naturally be surprised by our reply, saying that the answer is not what you asked. However, besides this kind of reply, we can't think of a "Thousand-Handed, Thousand-Eyed Avalokitesvara Bodhisattva" kind of "rescuing from suffering and difficulties" method.
