Education News

Important News

Jiangsu Education Director Zhou Fohai

Inspects Education in Southern Jiangsu (2)

Speaks to Education Community in Danyang at Noon

Arrives in Changzhou in the Evening and Inspects Self-Study at Jiangsu Changzhou High School

(Special Correspondent from Changzhou) It was reported yesterday that the Jiangsu Education Director Zhou Fohai and his party inspected education in Danyang. Today (the 22nd), they continued their inspection in Danyang. At 8:00 AM, they departed for the County Experimental Elementary School to observe the school buildings and equipment. He also reviewed various administrative records and student grades, making corrections to spelling and arithmetic exercises. At 9:00 AM, he inspected physical education in the third grade, combined first and second semester of the kindergarten Chinese language class, combined spring and autumn first grade Chinese language class, autumn second grade Chinese language class, autumn third grade Chinese language class, spring third and fourth grade Chinese language classes, spring fifth grade Chinese language class, autumn fifth grade Chinese language class, and autumn sixth grade arithmetic class. Then he went to the County Mingfeng Elementary School and gave instructions on the format of the school diary and various forms. He inspected the sixth-grade Chinese language class, the fifth-grade Chinese language class, the fourth-grade drawing class, the combined first and second grade Chinese language class, and the third-grade arithmetic class. Afterwards, he went to the County Normal School Affiliated Elementary School, providing guidance on experimental work, and also giving detailed instructions on spelling corrections and administrative facilities. He inspected the third grade's general knowledge class, the fourth grade's Chinese language class, the combined first and second grade's singing and games class, the fifth grade's arithmetic class, and the sixth grade's history class. By this time, it was nearly noon, and he returned to his residence for lunch. At 2:00 PM, Section Chiefs Chen and Xiang went to the Bureau of Education to inquire in detail about the operations of various schools and social education institutions in each district from the Education Committee members, and to discuss methods for improvement. At 3:00 PM, Director Zhou and Director Yi went to the County Experimental Elementary School to give speeches to more than one hundred teachers and education administrators in the urban area. First, Director Wang Mingji of the Bureau of Education gave a speech, and Director Zhou took the stage to speak, dividing his speech into two main points: service spirit and teaching methods. The service spirit was further divided into self-respect, self-encouragement, and self-love. The teaching methods were also divided into three points: promoting national spirit, emphasizing life training, and promoting livelihood education. His words were encouraging and sincere, and all the listeners were moved. Then, Section Chief Xiang gave a speech, proposing two points: loyalty to one's job and efforts to study, giving detailed explanations and very thorough guidance. Section Chief Chen reported on the methods for improving the Private School Propaganda Week and the points that elementary school colleagues should reflect on in a timely manner. Director Yi spoke on the issue of youth ideological guidance. Finally, Director Wang expressed his gratitude on behalf of the entire group. After the meeting, they returned to rest briefly and then took the 6:00 PM train to Changzhou, arriving at the station at 7:10 PM. County Magistrate Zhang Pengyi, Education Director Yang Haoming, County Supervisor Sun Youguang, and others greeted them. After getting off the train, they went directly to Jiangsu Changzhou High School to inspect students' self-study, inspecting each room. He gave many instructions on cleanliness and other matters, and also inspected the dormitory, inquiring with the staff of the Training Department about the students' living conditions and the implementation of the integration of education and training. At 9:30 PM, he went to the Da Min Hotel to rest. It is said that he will continue to inspect in Changzhou tomorrow. (Sent on March 22nd)

Report on the Ministry of Education's Supervisor's Inspection of Education in Jiangxi (Continued)

12. The aforementioned middle schools are quite attentive to science, and for the sake of preparing students for further studies, they often use original English textbooks in various subjects to seek convenience. In practice, due to language problems, it is inevitable that the progress of the subjects is slowed down. Methods should be immediately taken to use Chinese textbooks, focusing on specialized terminology in various subjects to seek practicality.

13. The various middle schools still do not pay enough attention to physical education and military training, resulting in students having no habit of exercise. There are not many types of extracurricular activities, and guidance is also inadequate.

14. The majority of private middle schools have simple buildings and equipment, lax teaching, and the quality of students seems to be lacking. They should be banned. The provincial normal school has a good environment and is well-managed.

15. Public and private elementary schools, with the exception of the provincial capital's experimental elementary school, kindergarten, girls' middle school experimental elementary school, and one or three church elementary schools, have overly simple equipment and unclean school buildings. Children have mostly not developed clean habits. The classroom floors are full of light snot and scraps of paper, and the desks, chairs, and walls are covered in chalk, which is unsightly. Strict training should be given to pay attention to school and personal hygiene.

16. Teaching methods are biased towards rote learning, and textbooks are used rigidly. There are no specimens, models, instruments, or other items to assist, and there are no opportunities for on-site observation and experimentation. Therefore, children have no concept of nature other than the words in books.

17. The layout of lighting and the height of desks and chairs in various elementary schools mostly fail to meet the principles of education. Teachers' lecturing tones are too loud, which interferes with the coursework in other classrooms.

18. Most school labor practices are limited to gardening and cooperative societies, with ordinary results. Children also lack a clear understanding of the meaning of cooperative societies. Labor activities should be increased, and teachers should provide practical guidance.

19. The preparation and content of statistical charts and graphs in various schools are mostly lacking in refinement. They are often overly artistic and lose the meaning of the charts and graphs.

20. The public education museum's location is too small, and the branch reading rooms are mostly simple and not suitable for public reading. Although there are many items on display in the exhibition halls, there are not many that are fresh, eye-catching, and arranged neatly and legally. Among them, the students' grade products are the most outdated and should be collected and added at any time to arouse the interest of the audience.

21. The Jiangxi Province's education funding of over two million yuan per year seems to be excessive for elementary schools and scholarship subsidies and insufficient for social education. It should be redistributed according to needs to seek balanced development. At the same time, the funding for local education is only over eight hundred thousand yuan, which is far from enough.

22. There are too many ordinary middle schools, which cannot meet the actual needs. Subsidies should be stopped for private schools that are poorly managed, and they should be ordered to close. The Department of Education must formulate an overall plan to add or convert vocational schools in stages.

23. Various levels of schools fail to effectively conduct physical and mental cultivation and youth guidance. Attention should be paid to avoid young people being affected by a bad environment and falling into the realm of dangerous thoughts and behaviors.

24. After the Department of Education strictly prohibited teachers at all levels from taking part-time jobs last year, the majority of teachers are now full-time, and their teaching spirit is also better than before, which can serve as a model for other provinces.

Regulations for Primary and Secondary Schools, Normal Schools, and Vocational Schools (5)

Chapter 7: Facilities

Article 43: Middle school sites must have sufficient area, and their environment must be suitable for moral and sanitary conditions.

Article 44: Middle schools should have the following essential places: (1) Ordinary classrooms; (2) Special classrooms (for physics, chemistry, biology, drawing, music, and other teaching purposes); (3) Workshops (prioritize setting up metalworking workshops), farms, cooperatives, or home economics practice rooms (depending on the types of labor courses offered and the school environment, provide one or more); (4) Sports grounds (a gymnasium should be provided if possible); (5) Library or reading room; (6) Instrument, medicine, specimen, and chart room; (7) Physical education equipment room; (8) Self-study room; (9) Auditorium; (10) Student achievement display room; (11) Extracurricular activity workshop; (12) Office (staff should work in the same room and should not occupy excellent buildings within the school); (13) Student dormitory; (14) Faculty dormitory (faculty housing should be provided if possible); (15) Dining hall; (16) Bathrooms; (17) Storage room; (18) Campus; (19) Other.

Article 45: School buildings should be sturdy, simple, practical, and should use domestic materials.

Article 46: The machinery, medicines, basic materials, charts, machines, and devices for teaching each subject must be sufficient for the needs of teaching each subject. Among the equipment mentioned above, such as instruments, specimens, and books, those that can be self-made should be made jointly by teachers and students as much as possible.

Article 47: The books in the middle school library must be sufficient for teachers and students to use for reference and reading. Multiple copies of those frequently used by students for reference should especially be provided.

Article 48: Middle schools should have the following registers and books:

(1) Laws and statistics related to middle schools; (2) School rules (including all school regulations, rules, and procedures); (3) Course schedule for each grade level, weekly teaching schedule for each class in each semester, and a list of textbooks used in each class; (4) Teacher and staff resumes, subject assignment and teaching schedule, teaching progress plan book, teaching progress record book; (5) Student enrollment register, attendance book, leave of absence book, conduct evaluation book, reward and punishment registration book, academic transcript, physical examination form; (6) Library catalog, instrument catalog, specimen catalog, equipment catalog, medicine catalog; (7) Property catalog; (8) Budget statement, final account statement, various accounting registers and books; (9) School diary book, grade level diary book; (10) Minutes of various meetings; (11) Other.

Article 49: Middle school equipment standards will be determined separately.

Chapter 8: Grades and Examinations

Article 50: Middle school student grades are divided into three categories: academic performance, conduct, and physical education.

Article 51: Academic performance is assessed in the following four ways: (1) Daily assessment; (2) Occasional tests; (3) Semester exams; (4) Graduation exams.

Article 52: The methods of daily assessment are as follows, and they should be used appropriately according to the nature of each subject: (1) Oral Q&A; (2) Exercises and practice; (3) Experiments and internships; (4) Reading reports; (5) Compositions; (6) Quizzes; (7) Investigation and collection reports; (8) Other work reports; (9) Labor operations.

Article 53: Occasional tests should be conducted by teachers of each subject at any time during teaching hours, without prior notice to students. Each subject should hold at least two or more such tests per semester.

Article 54: Semester exams should be conducted at the end of each semester after the completion of teaching each subject, based on the course content learned during the semester. Classes may be suspended for one to two days before the exam to allow students to review.

Article 55: Graduation exams should be conducted after the completion of three academic years, covering all courses learned in junior high or senior high. Classes may be suspended for three to four days before the exam to allow students to review. The timing of the graduation entrance examination should be after the completion of the school's graduation exams.

Article 56: Daily assessment grades and occasional test grades are combined to form the regular grade for each subject. Daily assessment grades account for two-thirds of the regular grade, and occasional test grades account for one-third.

Article 57: Regular grades and semester exam grades are combined to form the semester grade for each subject. Regular grades account for three-fifths of the semester grade, and semester exam grades account for two-fifths.

In the second semester of the third year of middle school, semester exams may be waived, and the regular grade for each subject may be used as the semester grade.

Article 58: The average of each student's semester grades in all subjects is that student's semester average. The average of each student's semester averages for the first and second semesters is that student's academic year average.

Article 59: The average of each student's academic year averages and their graduation exam grades are combined to form that student's graduation grade. The average of the academic year averages accounts for three-fifths of the graduation grade, and the graduation exam grades account for two-fifths.

Article 60: Students whose conduct grade or physical education grade is failing may not advance or graduate.

Article 61: Students whose absences in each subject reach one-third or more of the total teaching hours for that subject in each semester may not participate in the semester exam for that subject.

Article 62: Students who have no semester grade in a subject or have failing grades in three or more subjects, or who have only two subjects with no semester grade or failing grades, but those subjects are any two of the four subjects of Chinese, English, Mathematics, and Labor in junior high, or any two of the five subjects of Chinese, English, Mathematics, Physics, and Chemistry in senior high, should be demoted to a lower semester of the grade. If there is no equivalent grade in the school, a transfer certificate may be issued.

Article 63: Students who have no semester grade in a subject or have a failing grade in only one subject, or who have two subjects with no semester grade or failing grades, but those subjects are not as specified in the preceding article, should be allowed to attend the original grade as an auditor in the following semester and find a way to make up the deficient subjects. After passing the make-up semester exam, they will be officially promoted. If they still fail, they should repeat the original grade in the following academic year. However, this make-up exam and repeating a grade are limited to one time. If they still cannot advance, a certificate of completion will be issued, and they will be required to withdraw.

Article 64: Students whose failing grades in the graduation exam are in three or more subjects, or who have only two failing grades, but those subjects are any two of the four subjects of Chinese, English, Mathematics, and Labor in junior high, or any two of the five subjects of Chinese, English, Mathematics, Physics, and Chemistry in senior high, should be required to repeat a grade for one academic year. However, this repeating a grade is limited to one time. If they still cannot graduate, a certificate of completion will be issued, and they will be required to withdraw.

Article 65: Students whose failing grades in the graduation exam are in one subject, or who have two failing grades, but those subjects are not as specified in the preceding article, should be allowed to take a make-up exam once. If they still cannot pass, they should be handled according to the procedures in the preceding article.

Article 66: Methods for assessing conduct and physical education grades will be determined separately.

Article 67: The methods for calculating academic performance should be stipulated by the education administrative agencies of each province and city and submitted to the Ministry of Education for approval. For the purpose of educational experiments, each middle school may adopt other methods in addition to the calculation methods stipulated by the main education administrative agency, but it must be submitted to the Ministry of Education for approval.

Chapter 9: Academic Year, Semesters, and Holidays

Article 68: The academic year begins on August 1 and ends on July 31 of the following year.

Article 69: One academic year is divided into two semesters. From August 1 to January 31 of the following year is the first semester or the fall semester. From February 1 to July 31 is the second semester or the spring semester. For grades that start in the spring, the second semester of the current academic year is the fall semester, and the first semester of the next academic year is the spring semester. Each province should designate a number of provincial middle schools in appropriate locations to concurrently offer grades that start in the spring.

Article 70: The holiday dates for middle schools will be determined separately.

Article 71: Middle schools may not take holidays other than those stipulated by laws and regulations.

Chapter 10: Admission, Transfer, Leave of Absence, Reinstatement, Withdrawal, and Graduation

Article 72: The qualifications for admission to junior high school are elementary school graduation, and the qualifications for admission to senior high school are junior high school graduation. All must pass the entrance examination. The proportion of new students admitted to middle schools with equivalent qualifications should not exceed 20% of the total enrollment for senior high and should not exceed 30% for junior high. The education administrative agencies of each province and city should determine this based on local conditions and report it to the Ministry of Education for record.

Article 73: If a middle school student passes the semester or academic year-end exam and needs to transfer to another school, or if the situation stipulated in Article 62 occurs, they may request the school to issue a transfer certificate.

Article 74: If there are vacancies in grades above the second semester of middle school, transfer students may be accepted before the beginning of the semester or academic year. These transfer students must have a transfer certificate or transcript from another middle school that matches the semester and must still pass a grade level placement exam.

Article 75: Middle school students may request a leave of absence for one semester or one academic year due to special physical or family circumstances.

Article 76: Students who have completed their leave of absence may request reinstatement and enroll in the grade level that matches their original semester or academic year.

Article 77: Middle school students who have special physical or family circumstances and whose reasons are confirmed to be legitimate by a guarantor may request the school to approve their withdrawal.

Article 78: Students who have been expelled from school may not be issued a transfer certificate or a certificate of completion.

Article 79: Students who have completed the required years of study, passed the graduation exam, and passed the entrance examination are allowed to graduate and will be given a graduation certificate by the school.

Chapter 11: Fees and Scholarships

Article 80: The types of fees charged to students by middle schools are as follows: (1) Tuition; (2) Library fee; (3) Physical education fee. The library fee mentioned above is specifically for purchasing books that students need for reference in the library, and the physical education fee is specifically for providing students with sports, excursions, trips, and health supplies. Neither may be used for other purposes.

Article 81: Private middle schools that have dormitories may charge boarding students a reasonable boarding fee.

Beijing Municipal Government Orders Schools to Coordinate Military Training

On the 23rd, the Municipal Government ordered all registered public and private high schools and above in the city to request assistance from nearby military units for training in accordance with the National Military Education Regulations promulgated by the Training and Supervision Department.

Soochow University of Education

Affiliated Rural Handicraft Training Class

Training in three crafts: straw, rattan willow, and bamboo wood

For several years, the Jiangsu Provincial Soochow University of Education has achieved remarkable results in promoting livelihood education for the people, such as the organization of cooperatives, the introduction of improved seeds, and the raising of bees, chickens, pigs, cattle, and sheep. The nearby people have benefited greatly. It is learned that in order to promote rural side occupations, the college has recently established a rural handicraft training class, recruiting students to provide training in straw, rattan willow, and bamboo wood crafts. Students must be recommended by the Jiangsu Provincial Social Education Agency or other educational agencies. If they are not recommended by the above agencies, they must be introduced by the college's faculty members before they can be admitted. The quota is tentatively set at 15 students. Classes will begin on April 13 and will last for two months. Those who pass the examination will be given a certificate. In terms of fees, each student must pay 4 yuan for consumption expenses and 12 yuan for food expenses, which must be prepaid upon admission. In recent days, social education agencies from various places have sent letters recommending students for admission. It is expected that the training results of this class will be excellent.

Nanjing Ginling College is known in society for its improvement of agricultural and forestry enterprises. It is learned that the school is also very concerned about vocational education for women. Sports Meet Demonstration Teaching Materials

First Section: Limb Exercises (1) Step forward with the left foot, raise both arms to the sides; (2) Raise both arms to the sides and upwards, clap hands together above the head; (3) Return to the position of (1); (4) Return the left foot and arms to the original position; (5) (6) (7) (8) Repeat the same with the right foot stepping forward. Do a total of thirty-two beats. Students chant.

Second Section: Chest Expansion Exercise (1) Raise both arms forward to shoulder height; (2) Bend both arms at the chest, fist hands (upper and lower arms at shoulder height, backs of hands facing outward), and forcefully pull open to the rear while expanding the chest; (3) Return to the position of (1); (4) Return the arms to the original position; (5) (6) (7) (8) Same as above. Do a total of thirty-two beats. Students do not chant. At the last beat, jump feet apart and place hands in an axe-gripping shape on the left shoulder.

Third Section: Abdominal Exercise (1) Bend the upper body forward and downward, chop both arms forward and downward to below the hips; (2) Return the upper body to the original position, place hands in an axe-gripping shape on the shoulder; (3) Bend the upper body forward and downward, chop both arms forward and downward to below the hips; (4) Return the upper body to the original position, place hands in an axe-gripping shape on the left shoulder; (5) (6) (7) (8) Same as above. Do a total of thirty-two beats. Students do not chant. At the last beat, fist hands, bend arms at the elbows and place them at the waist, making a fist-holding posture (upper arms vertical, feet still apart).

Total of 162 Schools Suspended

65,635 Students Out of School

2,985 Unemployed Teachers and Staff

When the Municipal Government bureaus prepared to participate in the Chicago World's Fair celebrating the centenary of progress in America, the Municipal Education Bureau compiled statistics on the major impacts of the Japanese military invasion of Shanghai on citywide education, with Chinese and Western comparisons, for publicity purposes. However, the order was then given to stop participation. Nevertheless, the statistics have long been compiled. The most important of these, comparing before and after the war, are extracted below.

Fourth Section: Torso Rotation Exercise (1) Rotate the upper body to the left, and simultaneously thrust the right fist to the left (arm level); (2) Return the upper body to the center, retract the right fist; (3) Rotate the upper body to the right, and simultaneously thrust the left fist to the right; (4) Return the upper body to the center, retract the left fist; (5) (6) (7) (8) Same as above. Do a total of thirty-two beats. Students do not chant. At the last beat, return to standing at attention.

Fifth Section: Waist Exercise (1) Place hands on hips, left foot in a left lunge; (2) Lean the upper body to the left; (3) Return the upper body to upright; (4) Retract the left foot, put down hands; (5) Place hands on hips, right foot in a right lunge; (6) Lean the upper body to the right; (7) Return the upper body to upright; (8) Retract the right foot, put down hands. Do a total of thirty-two beats.

Sixth Section: Fast Exercise (1) Bend both arms forward to shoulder height, cross arms over the chest (left arm on top, right arm on the bottom), jump feet left and right alternately (left foot in front, right foot in back); (2) Jump feet apart, separate both arms left and right, forming a lateral arm raise; (3) Same as (1), but switch to right arm on top, right foot in front; (4) Same as (2); (5) (6) (7) (8) Same as above. Do a total of twenty-two beats. At the last beat, jump to a standing at attention position, stomp feet sixteen beats.

Seventh Section: Breathing Exercise (1) (2) Raise arms from the sides upward, inhale; (3) (4) Lower arms from the sides downward, exhale; (5) (6) (7) (8) Same as above. Do a total of thirty-two beats.

Sponsored by the Municipal Education Bureau

Shuttlecock Kicking Competition

All-American Indoor Games

Creating Three World Records

60 Meters　　　　6.7 seconds

65 Meter Hurdles　8.6 seconds

3000 Meter Steeplechase　9 minutes 6.1 seconds

(New York Dispatch) The All-American Indoor Games, organized by the American Amateur Athletic Association, created three new world records. McCade University's black athlete, Motogaifu, broke the old 60-meter record with 6.7 seconds, the old record being 7.2 seconds held by Topino. Topino was second on this day, and Wickoff was third. Also, in the 65-meter hurdles, New York's Piert set a new world record with 8.6 seconds. Keller's 3000-meter steeplechase also broke the world record. The results of the games are listed below:

Spring and Autumn

The Six Gentlemen

— Yongzi

丨丨Everyone is making much ado about nothing丨丨

The six English gentlemen, stirring up trouble in Soviet Russia, were to be charged with counter-revolutionary crimes by the Soviets—impartial and without bias, one bullet for each. This greatly alarmed England, which hastily issued a protest. Of course, England's protest was one hundred and twenty-four times more impressive than China's "responsibility lies with your country" tune. Unexpectedly, the protest hit a rubber nail in Soviet Russia, resulting in a nose-bruising encounter, as the protest proved ineffective. The case of these six gentlemen has unexpectedly stirred great emotion within me.

As I, an ignoramus, understand it, a counter-revolutionary invariably schemes to overthrow the government of the country in which they reside. I recall that a couple of unknown nationality established a base in Shanghai a few years ago, spreading communism, inciting labor unrest, organizing worker-peasant armies, and plotting to subvert the Chinese government to create a Soviet regime. Ironclad evidence was presented, and they were caught red-handed. If such a thing were to happen in another country, humph, needless to say, fifty pairs out of a hundred would have been killed. But China, with the magnanimity of a prime minister who can sail a boat even in his belly and a magistrate who shows leniency in his writings, sentenced them to life imprisonment, allowing them to live out their days as machines digesting milk and bread. In the end, China maintained its great-nation demeanor, and did not hold petty grievances against small people. England, because Soviet Russia was about to punish the six gentlemen, considered the matter grave and international relations strained. In my opinion, this is making a mountain out of a molehill. Why? Well, Chinese expatriates in Japan and Korea are treated in the same way as English expatriates in Russia—no extraterritoriality. Therefore, when our Chinese compatriots commit crimes under Japanese jurisdiction, the Japanese kill Chinese people without asking questions, and the Chinese have no resentment for the deaths. Even Koreans and Taiwanese who have naturalized and live in Shanghai are often arrested and punished by the Japanese. Has China ever turned blue in the face, or have Sino-Japanese relations ever been strained? This alone is enough to show that China does not like to cause trouble and is not as afraid of peace as others.

Shanghai Morning Talk

— Baihe

丨The Three Sights of Dawn for the Early Morning Watchman丨

Mr. Zhang Ruogu wrote several "Shanghai Night Talks." It seems that Mr. Zhang leads a "nightingale life," so he has a lot of material for night talks. I, on the other hand, am an "early morning watchman" all year round. By the time Mr. Zhang is yawning and putting his head on the pillow, I am already yawning, preparing to hobble around and inspect the streets. So, after reading "Shanghai Night Talks," I feel itchy and want to try a "Shanghai Morning Talk."

Those who live the same life as I do are the silk factory workers. No matter where I go, there are always several of them walking along, carrying small lunch baskets, chattering like orioles and swallows. I glance at them, and they also look at me with sympathy, perhaps silently singing in their hearts, "Fate, a chance encounter..." Although I have never asked them their names, whether they are Sister Azhao or Sister Aqiao.

Standing under the eaves at the corner of the street is the "police officer." When you walk past him, he will suddenly stir in the darkness and give you a big fright. So, when I walk past such places, I always pretend to cough three steps away as a signal. The "police officer" is startled first, then straightens up and salutes me. This is called preemptive strike.

The early market on Wangping Street, I'm not lying, is three minutes earlier than the one at the Sixteen Pups. Every morning when I pass Wangping Street, old men, women with bound feet, young girls, and children, all kinds of newspaper vendors are carrying bags, looking like they are going on a pilgrimage. And their spirit of vying for the lead is like the big knife team of the 19th Route Army. Once they get the newspapers, the way they squat on the terrazzo and fold and distribute them, I don't know what to call it, so I call it calmly preparing for battle.

These are the three sights of dawn in Shanghai, which are not easily appreciated by Shanghainese people. In addition, the dim, sleepy lights, the rickshaw pullers with hunched heads and necks, and the homeless sleeping under the overhanging buildings can only be seen by the "early morning watchmen." As for dumping chamber pots and vegetable markets, these things always happen after dawn, lagging behind.

Modern Conversation

— Zhao Ziming

(A) Nowadays, so-called modern women can't do anything practically.

(B) Why do you say that?

(A) Look! They wear high heels, and when they walk, they always walk on their toes. Isn't that ironclad proof?

(B) I say that nowadays, so-called modern men are all slippery.

(A) Why do you say that, too?

(B) Look! Their mustaches are coated with Stancon until they gleam. Flies will slip if they fly on it. Isn't that proof that they're slippery?

(A, B) Haha, modern men and women, so that's how it is?!

Long Novel

The Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Two: Dark Thoughts in a Humble Room, Zheng Secretly Admires the Robust Old Man; Choosing a Good Match, Bitterly Criticizing the Poor Girl

He's getting on in years and should settle down with a wife. Whether she's traditional or modern, we as his elder brother and sister-in-law shouldn't object. But how could he have fallen for a working girl? That girl has only a widowed mother, and their family is so poor that they only have an earthen bed left. If he gets too close to her, it's bound to lead to jokes. Just now, he borrowed the excuse of delivering clothes and came into the yard. I told him Jingzhi wasn't home and sent him away. While Mrs. Gan sorted through the clothes, she listened to her husband's words. At this point, her face darkened, and she kept looking at the trunk but raised her voice, saying, "This is only the fault of our own people, not others. You should call Jingzhi and give him a good scolding. That girl helps me with my work, and sometimes she doesn't even ask for money. She's a good person. As long as Jingzhi doesn't tempt her, she won't be embarrassed to keep coming." Houzhi thought what she said was reasonable. He put a cigarette in his mouth, put his hands behind his back, and walked towards Jingzhi's room. Jingzhi had already put the newly made robe over his cotton gown, intending to go out. He bumped into his older brother and thought he could show off his frugality, so he smiled and said, "I've also put on a blue cloth gown." Houzhi coldly said, "You shouldn't just focus on appearances when you do things. Does wearing a blue cloth gown make someone a thrifty person?" Because Jingzhi relied on his older brother's influence to get a job at the River Conservancy Bureau, he didn't dare to disobey his brother's words, so he blushed and stood to the side, saying nothing. Houzhi straightened his face and said, "I know you don't care about the clothes themselves, but about the person who made them. When you're working outside, you need to maintain your status. Confucius said that a gentleman without dignity is not imposing. We may not be a very noble family, but our friends are all respectable. Just take your sister-in-law's family as an example. What kind of people are they? You're so hopeless, getting so close to a working girl, coming and going, being very affectionate. I can't believe you have the nerve to keep running to her house. I heard that her family is so poor that they only have a bare earthen bed, and the house is as dark as a dungeon. What do you mean by running to her house all the time? If people see you, how can you face them?" (21)

The Training of Speech Summer

— Wu

丨It's a pity the person is already dead, it just got added in!丨

A friend of mine once asked me: Why don't you like to talk more? At first, I wondered why he asked me this, but a flash of inspiration told me that my speech had never offended him, and he often laughed when he heard my words. After he asked me this, I felt somewhat fortunate for myself, knowing that I used to talk to him a lot, but fortunately I never clashed with him. I also knew that I was indeed willing to talk less.

If one is blessed by nature to not like talking much, or if one has gained the skill through training, such a person should always be fortunate. My intention is not to call you to refute me, "Then everyone should become a mute." Mutes, of course, are different from people who can speak. If everyone were a mute, I wouldn't speak either, and no one would find the term "mute" to contrast with my speech. Before everyone becomes a mute, those who speak less should always be fortunate.

Even when the "mute" is still an uncommon reality, a person who can speak pretending to be a mute is ultimately more useful than the many senseless things of unfinished poetry or the showing off of a self-braggart. Even if one is ridiculed, it's still cheaper by comparison, speaking scientifically.

The best thing is that, as a Chinese citizen, one should have training in speech. We are a famous ancient country with flourishing culture and education. You shouldn't be an unlucky person who steps into a teahouse or wine shop and faces "No discussion of state affairs." Ancient poetry says: "Each person sweeps the snow from their own doorstep, don't mind the frost on others' roofs." The sage's words: "Prudent self-preservation." You should know the background of these sayings. Your motives are good, your attitude is bright, your reasons are sufficient. But, but the world will have an opposite side, and you will receive an unexpectedly distant answer representing another truth.

If you want to walk the path of luck, remember to turn your speech into a circle, be careful to keep a taboo mentality, your mentality must forget this era and must retreat to the autocratic era, just like avoiding the "sage's name" in the autocratic era. For example, if the person across from you likes to smoke opium, you must not reveal any accent that mentions the harm of opium, and of course, don't talk about Lin Zexu in a disjointed way: when you see him engrossed in inhaling clouds and spitting mist, with a leisurely will, you should praise the efficacy of opium; you say that opium can stop abdominal pain and diarrhea, and can clear the mind and refresh the spirit, which is to implement one's own claim and win the favor of the listener.

Please admit it, because in the world I have never seen someone use a disdainful look to receive the flattery of others, and listen with a natural smile to the well-intentioned missed criticisms of others. In foreign countries, there are many famous movie stars who may show such wonderful expressions on the screen, but it's a pity that the flashes are fleeting, and it's not clear to see. It seems that articles like "The Inheritance of the Great Man" have also seen very good literary descriptions, but it's a pity that the person is already dead!

Voice of National Salvation

Proposal for an Open University (Part 2)

— Zhang Yizeng

Now, let's take an example to illustrate the organization of each department. Suppose we invite Mr. Ma Yinchu to be the director of the Economics Department, giving lectures on Banking from 8:00 AM to 9:00 AM. The so-called lecture is to broadcast the lecture using a lecture film, and Professor Ma does not have to be present in person. From 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM is Principles of Economics, from 10:00 AM to 11:00 AM is Accounting, from 11:00 AM to 12:00 PM is Statistics, from 1:00 PM to 2:00 PM is International Trade, from 2:00 PM to 3:00 PM is Commercial Law, from 3:00 PM to 4:00 PM is Economic Organization, from 4:00 PM to 5:00 PM is Labor Issues, from 5:00 PM to 6:00 PM is Commercial History, from 6:00 PM to 7:00 PM is Commercial Credit Issues, from 7:00 PM to 8:00 PM is Foreign Exchange, from 8:00 PM to 9:00 PM is Economic Issues, and from 9:00 PM to 10:00 PM is Economic Overview. Every day, the Economics Department's radio station can invite an experienced businessman to report on the daily commercial situation. This is the Economics Department's broadcasting station. If there are new academic theories, experts can be invited to the station to give lectures. In addition, we can set up a Department of Chinese Studies, a Department of English Studies, a Department of Philosophy, a Department of Law, a Department of Education, a Department of Psychology, etc. As for science, which emphasizes experimentation, we can assume that students attend lectures every Monday, Wednesday, and Friday, and go to the Public Education Center to experiment on Tuesdays, Thursdays, and Saturdays, with teaching assistants guiding everything. All students who experiment must pay a deposit to compensate for damage to equipment in the laboratory. Last year, Mr. Wu Yunfu donated several free academic places in the field of chemistry, and many people took the exam, which shows that there are indeed many people in China who are eager to learn. The number of students admitted was very small, but with the Open University, wouldn't all these eager-to-learn students be able to study? As for students studying engineering, they can imitate the Cincinnati University's six-week study, six-week internship, and the method of internship is even more appropriate.

As for the examination, we can imitate the British degree examination. Before the examination, each student must have a general examination, such as Chinese, English, and Mathematics. Only those who pass the general examination can be allowed to take the degree examination. Those who fail the general examination cannot join the degree examination. The degree examination requires testing everything from beginning to end in a department. For those who study philosophy, everything related to philosophy itself and all courses related to philosophy must be tested. If this is done, the diploma of the Open University will be valuable. Someone may also ask, "After the Open University is established, won't all the existing public and private universities have to close?" I say no. There are still those with family assets who want to enjoy the scenery of the university, while the Ministry of Education can try its best to ban business-style universities. A classmate of mine graduated from a university in Shanghai, and the title of bachelor was engraved on his name card. I talked with him for a moment and realized that this is what a university student is. Another university student is a Bachelor of Arts, but what he says and writes cannot be understood by foreigners. I asked him how he was able to graduate. He said, "The school is fuzzy, and so am I." In the past, someone also asked, "After the Open University is established, won't the professors lose their jobs?" I say no. The money from opening the school can be used to open middle schools and elementary schools, and the professors can be invited to be principals and teachers, so that they can also have a place to live.

Internal strife and foreign troubles will pass sooner or later. Only schools run by the Chinese themselves can cultivate talent for China's construction. Schools run by foreigners are not up to the task. Is there any foreigner who is truly and sincerely helping China? What they do is mostly for their own interests. Chinese people, quickly get up and run on the road to construction. Those with money should use money to build, those with strength should use strength to save the country, and those with knowledge should work hard in knowledge. With the thousands of years of glory of our China, there may be a possibility of revival in this time of hardship. (If you have any comments, please send them to China Post Office Box 702.)

Free Talk

Literature of Stanching Cries

— He Jiagan

Three years ago, when the "Nationalist Literature" proponents were banging gongs and drums, an article titled "The Blood of the Yellow Race" stated their highest aspiration was to follow in the footsteps of Batu Khan, grandson of Genghis Khan, to annihilate "the Oros." The Oros are the current Soviet Russia. At that time, some people pointed out that the current Batu's army is the Japanese army, and before "the Western Expedition," they must first conquer China and turn it into a slave to the army.

When we are conquered ourselves, it is very painful for all but a few people. This is exemplified by the loss of the three northeastern provinces and the bombings of Shanghai. Among all living people, there are very few who are not sad and indignant. But this sorrow and indignation greatly hinders the future "Western Expedition." Thus came "The Destruction of Greater Shanghai," which used numbers to tell readers that China's military force was definitely not as good as Japan's, to calm everyone down; and believed that it was better to die than to live ("The death of the 19th Route Army is a warning that we live miserably, without interest!"), but that defeat was even better than victory ("The victory of the 19th Route Army can only increase our complacency, complacency, and pride!"). In short, it is good to die in battle, but it is especially good to be defeated. The Battle of Shanghai was a complete success for China.

Now the second step has begun. According to Central News Agency reports, Japan has a conspiracy to sign a "Commonwealth of China Empire Secret Agreement" with Manchuria. The first article of that plan is: "There are only two types of countries in the world now, one is capitalist, England, America, Japan, Italy, France, and the other is communist, Soviet Russia. Now to resist Soviet Russia, Sino-Japanese alliance… is the only way to succeed" (see Shen Bao, March 19).

They want to "ally." This time it is a complete success for China and Japan, the second step in moving from "The Destruction of Greater Shanghai" to the road of "Blood of the Yellow Race."

Of course, some places are being bombed, but Shanghai, since being bombed, has had more than a year, but some people do not realize the inevitable steps of the "Western Expedition," and it seems that they have not completely forgotten the sorrow and indignation of the previous year. This sorrow and indignation greatly hinders the current "alliance." In this situation, what is born in response is to give people a little refreshment and consolation, like the literature of "chili and olives." This may be a cure for depression. Why? Because "chili is spicy, but it won't kill you, olives are bitter, but there is a taste in the bitterness." Understanding this, one will know why coolies smoke opium.

Moreover, it is not only silent depression, but it is also said that chili can even stop "annoying cries." Mr. Wang Ci tells us in his famous article "Advocating Chili to Save the Country"!

"...Also, when northerners are in their mothers' arms, when they cry loudly, if the mother gives the child a spicy eggplant to bite, it can be very effective in stopping the crying immediately...

"The current China is like a northern baby crying loudly. If you want to stop his annoying cries, you only need to give him more spicy eggplants to bite." (Da Wan Bao Supplement No. 12)

Chili can stop a child's loud crying, which is unprecedented news. If it is true, then the Chinese are indeed a special "nation" different from others. However, it is also very clear to see that the intention of this "literature" is to give people a spice that will not kill them, "stop his annoying cries," and wait for Batu Khan.

However, this is ineffective, far less effective than "summary execution" for those who cry. What we need to guard against from now on is "exchanging glances on the road." We are waiting for literature that blinds the eyes.

"Mad Torrent" and "City Night"

— Xuan

The Mingxing and Lianhua film companies have both recently announced a "change in style." Mingxing's "Mad Torrent" and Lianhua's "City Night" are the latest representative works of the two companies.

Technically, because "Mad Torrent" takes the great flood of the previous year as its theme, and mainly focuses on mass struggle, it is not as easy to show off skill as "City Night," which mainly focuses on depicting the dark side of the city. If "City Night" is more popular with urban audiences, the reason may lie in this.

As for the content, if we only look at the descriptions of these two films, we may still feel that "City Night" is better (the description is really novel); but after watching it and thinking carefully, our opinion is different. "Mad Torrent" intersperses a love romance, with the daughter of a local tyrant falling in love with a village teacher who is a peasant leader; "City Night" also has a similar romance, with the son of a capitalist falling in love with a female worker. Both similarly express the struggle between "father and son" in the midst of love. However, these two romances are essentially different. In "Mad Torrent," what ignites the passion of the tyrant's daughter is the brave and bright personality of the other person; but in "City Night," what arouses the love of the capitalist's son is what? Judging from the plot, it is only shallow humanitarianism, or even the so-called mysterious and inexplicable love. The ending of "Mad Torrent," where the tyrant does not die from the anger of the masses, but from the flood, inevitably still has the feudal stench of "the net of heaven is vast"; but the ending of "City Night" puts forward the slogan of "going to the countryside to create a new life," which is seemingly true but actually false. Because rural bankruptcy is now an ironclad fact, the countryside is not a paradise!

The fact is that the countryside went bankrupt first, so the peasants left. The strong social reform policy inclination in "City Night" made the film drag out the slogan "go to the countryside" at the end, but it reversed the cause and effect of social phenomena, making the depiction of urban darkness in the entire film lose its meaning! It is precisely on this point that the essential differences in the meaning of "Mad Torrent" and "City Night" lie! Although "Mad Torrent" still has some shortcomings, it is still a film that exposes the darkness of society.

Letter from Mr. Liu Zongyuan

To Mr. Hu Huaichen, Editor of Free Talk: I have seen the two letters you published in Shen Bao and the article published in Min Bao. In your first letter, you seem to admit your mistake, and I admire your frankness. In your second letter, you say that because my article was not well written, it made you misunderstand. I can also admit this. My article may indeed be badly written because it is impossible to learn from the ancients well. However, the reason why my article was written that way was precisely because of the two intentions you mentioned: (1) the same noun is used too many times; (2) the same noun is too close together. Consider

(1) If I had written my first sentence honestly, it would have been: The mountain of Stone Fish. All stone. No large vegetation. The mountain is small and high, its shape like a standing fish, located west of Xian Yi, with a cave similar to Xian Yi.

There are two repetitions of "Xian Yi." Consider again

(2) If I had written my second sentence honestly, it would have been:

Huangxi is seventy li from the prefectural seat. Go six hundred steps south from Dongtun to Huangshen Temple. Above Huangshen Temple, two mountain walls stand...Above Huangshen Temple, Jieshui is eighty steps...

There are three repetitions of "Huangshen Temple." Therefore, I thought I should vary the style. In the first sentence, I used "Duo Zigui" to replace one of the "Xian Yi" characters, resulting in:

The mountain of Stone Fish, all stone, no large vegetation. The mountain is small and high, its shape like a standing fish, located west of Duo Zigui, with a cave similar to Xian Yi.

In the second sentence, I omitted the second and third instances of "Huangshen Temple." In the second instance of "Huangshen Temple," I omitted "Huangshen," leaving only the character "Temple"; in the third instance of "Huangshen Temple," I kept "Huangshen," omitting "Temple," resulting in: Huangxi is seventy li from the prefectural seat. Go six hundred steps south from Dongtun to Huangshen Temple. Above the Temple, two mountain walls stand...Above Huangshen, Jieshui is eighty steps...

This is the style I came up with. My style may not be well done, but I did change it this way. I hope you acknowledge this. You say that I didn't learn well from the ancients, which made you misunderstand, and this may be true, but it is also true that you misunderstood my article. Therefore, let's just cancel out the apology.

Liu Zongyuan (March 22nd) Editor's note: From Mr. Liu's letter, we can learn a small lesson, which is: blindly imitating the ancients is indeed not feasible. Because Mr. Liu imitated the "Classic of Mountains and Seas," he stubbornly changed his article with many unnecessary variations, causing Mr. Hu to misinterpret it and make some jokes, and also bothering Mr. Liu to personally point it out, wasting a lot of energy. What a pity! However, Mr. Liu's poor imitation of the ancients is one thing, and Mr. Hu's misunderstanding of Mr. Liu's article is another. Mr. Liu is not only not annoyed that his article was misunderstood, but also admits that he should not have imitated the ancients, which shows the ancient people's "modesty" and "willingness to accept good advice."

Parisian Chats

— Xiao Shijun, sent from Paris

(VII) Maeterlinck's Tragi-Comedy

Maeterlinck's name is known to many in the motherland. He is not only a great Belgian playwright, but also one of the most successful figures in the new romantic drama of the twentieth century. However, he himself also starred in a tragicomedy. We only learned a rough idea after Mrs. Georgette Leblanc published a memoir a couple of years ago. Last year, a friend, Gerand Harry, wrote a book called "The Life and Works of Maurice Maeterlinck" (La Vie et laeuvre de Maurice Macterlinck), a chapter of which also mentions this tragicomedy. The matter is as follows: In 1895, Maeterlinck met Mrs. Leblanc, a famous actress who admired him. Although he was thirty-four years old at the time, he had not yet formally married any other woman. Leblanc admired him very much, and he also loved Leblanc very much. Soon, they realized their plan to live together. Maeterlinck's early works were very pessimistic, such as "Princess Maleine," "The Intruder," "The Blind," and "Interior," all of which expressed terror of death and the mystery of fate. After living with Leblanc, "Aglavaine and Sélysette," published the following year, and "Monna Vanna" in 1902, changed from pessimism to optimism. Critics said that Maeterlinck underwent a transformation in his inner life because he lived with Leblanc. When they lived together, Mrs. Leblanc was just twenty years old. We can now see her admiration for Maeterlinck and Maeterlinck's love for her from the correspondence between the two excerpted in Mrs. Leblanc's "Memoirs." However, their friendship officially broke down in 1919 because Maeterlinck officially married a young woman who performed in the play with Mrs. Leblanc that year.

Mrs. Leblanc was born in Rouen. Her family was quite well-off. Her father was the manager of a shipping company. Because he was rich, he loved to collect antiques. Her brother was very fond of literature and art, and had written some novels. He had a great influence on her. The literary books that Mrs. Leblanc read as a child were all bought for her by her brother. He was the first to hear the name Maeterlinck from his mouth. He originally loved to read Maeterlinck's works. He told her that some people called Maeterlinck the Shakespeare of Belgium. So later, when Mrs. Leblanc went to the Belgian capital to perform, she wanted to find an opportunity to meet Maeterlinck. Finally, she saw Maeterlinck at the home of a famous lawyer. As soon as others announced Maeterlinck's name, she couldn't help but exclaim, "What a blessing, he is still so young!" Because before she met Maeterlinck, the famous lawyer, seeing that she was so infatuated with Maeterlinck, deliberately joked with her, saying, "You don't know, he is already an old man." Mrs. Leblanc immediately replied, "I don't care, he is my God."

According to her "Memoirs," her mother died when she was sixteen years old. After her mother's death, her father often lost his temper at home because of mourning. She was bored and eager to make an engagement with someone so that she could leave this depressing family. So she made a confused engagement with a Spanish boy. After the engagement, she discovered many bad things about this boy. Her father asked him to dissolve the engagement. This boy therefore committed suicide by taking poison. Harry, however, says that her husband was an adventurer, and because of other matters, he had to hide, and although it could be guessed that he was dead, there was no proof of death. In front of the law, she could not dissolve the engagement. The reason why she lived with Maeterlinck for twenty years without officially announcing her marriage to Maeterlinck was this. (To be continued)

Long Creation

The Crossroads of Time and Love

— Zhang Guanping

"Mr. Lin, don't treat me like a country bumpkin! This is terrible, Mr. Lin!"

She made a face at him again, followed by a charming smile.

"That's not what I meant. Because I only found out about this kind of thing just now, a professor told me."

"Then, Mr. Lin is a country bumpkin. Haha. I'll try it and see if it tastes good."

She unpacked a package, took out a piece, and immediately put it in her mouth.

"Mr. Lin, do you know that Westerners eat chewing gum before kissing?"

She said with a smile again. A little white foam flowed from her lips. Her impolite attitude caused some disgust in him.

"…………………………………………"

Haiquan just smiled and shook his head. At the same time, he secretly regretted that he missed the opportunity yesterday and did not kiss Mrs. Hezi. When he was sitting in the car, why didn't he try the taste of kissing the opposite sex?

"Mr. Lin, eat more, good K…i…ss!" She said, lowering her head.

"I don't have a target!"

He felt his cheeks were heating up, and he also smiled.

"Don't lie to me, Mr. Lin! Who doesn't know you have a lover! Tell me, what kind of beauty is your Sweet heart?…"

Haiquan thought, that's right, Cao Shiguang must have told his wife about seeing Mrs. Hezi in Zhaofeng Park yesterday.

"There's no such thing. There really isn't."

"Fortunately, someone saw it."

| Delivery Period Approaching, Some Covering of Short Positions in the Current Month |

Yesterday, at the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange, public bonds continued to rise, presumably because the war was calm, the situation in Tianjin has calmed down, and there are only 24 days left for futures trading in the current month. There is a gradual increase in short covering in the market, and there are also many bulls swapping positions. At the same time, large traders, designated as "32," are quite active. However, because the demand is strong, they have been unable to suppress the price. In the absence of changes in this environment, the time for the bulls and bears to test each other's strength is approaching. A close contest is likely to involve fierce competition. Yesterday's trading saw stronger gains in the spot market, with various bonds rising by about 3-4 "角" to 7-8 "角." Although the selling pressure from "32" was quite heavy, it was still insufficient to meet the demand. In the secondary market, the bulls swapped positions due to the favorable prices in the near and distant markets. "32" also sold off some positions. Human Bidding: A Squeeze

Our Troops at Xifengkou Tenaciously Defend Based on Natural Defenses

Chinese and Japanese Forces Each Hold One of the North and South Mountain Peaks

Enemy Retreats Twenty Miles from Luowenyu Shanzhayu

Enemy Assembles Outside Lengkou, Planning to Attack Our Rear

Japanese Rebel Allied Forces Attack Dongshangzhai and are Repelled

(Beiping) The Japanese army recently attacked Xifengkou. Fearing a counterattack from our forces at Shihe, they dispatched a large number of warships to the waters off Qinhuangdao to defend. Seeing that our forces at Shihe were changing defenses and showed no aggressive offensive posture, the Japanese warships left one after another, leaving only a few ships patrolling the coast near the Beining Railway. At the same time, they assembled a large force, such as the 16th Brigade of the Kawahara Unit and the 38th Division of the Nakamura Unit, outside Lengkou, launching a large-scale attack on Lengkou, plotting to attack the rear of Xifengkou. At the same time, the enemy has also been increasing troops in the Gubeikou area for days, and the enemy will advance to the left again to contain the Xifengkou route. However, our army has strict precautions on all routes. (24th Dispatch)

(Beiping) Xifengkou has a total of two mountain peaks. The north mountain peak is in the hands of the Japanese army, and the south mountain peak is still in the hands of our army. With a commanding view, Xifengkou is definitely not in danger. The 29th Army's office in Ping received a phone call from the front today. The Luowenyu and Shanzhayu areas have been calm for days, and the enemy has retreated to more than twenty miles away. According to reports, the enemy's rear is busy transporting boxes and objects to Chengde, seemingly retreating. (24th Dispatch)

(Beiping) Shang Zhen telegraphed from the 23rd that after the enemy in the Lengkou area arrived at Xiaojiayingzi, Commander Huang personally led a certain unit to fight against the enemy. The enemy gradually increased from morning to evening, reaching more than 2,000 infantrymen, more than a dozen mountain guns, several tanks, and more than a hundred armored vehicles. After a day of fierce fighting, the positions in Xiaojiaying and Madaogou were lost and regained more than ten times. Our army rushed out of the positions, destroying three tanks and seven armored vehicles. The enemy retreated to the highlands near Xiadahushan. Many corpses were left in the gully. Our army suffered casualties of more than a dozen officers and soldiers, and the investigation is underway. (24th Dispatch)

(Beiping) A certain regiment of our army outside Lengkou ambushed the enemy's positions on both flanks at dawn yesterday. The enemy's left wing was hit hard and showed signs of wavering. The fierce fighting lasted until noon before the ceasefire. In the stalemate, there were still minor skirmishes in the afternoon. Because of the repeated failed attacks on Xifengkou, the enemy has now mobilized the main force of three brigades to launch a general attack on Lengkou. There will be a major battle within days. If Lengkou is not defended, Xifengkou can be obtained without a fight. Shang will personally supervise the battle and has been bombed by enemy planes in Jinchangying in the mouth of the Lianri. (24th Dispatch)

(Beiping) Shang Zhen telegraphed on the 23rd that the enemy attacked several times at dawn on the 20th in the Jielingkou area and were all repelled. They continued to use a large number of planes in teams to bomb our positions. Our army's morale was high, and although there were many casualties, they were not moved at all. There were no changes in the Shihe, Shimenzhai, and Qinhuangdao areas. Commander Shang went to a certain battlefield in the afternoon because the war in the front was fierce. (24th Dispatch)

British Economic Panic and Unemployment (February 28th)

At the start of each new year, bankers always bring out their old clichés: "The turnaround has begun," "Prosperity is just around the corner." This year, 1933, they are saying the same thing. Reginald McKenna, the general manager of the influential British Midland Bank, said at the bank's shareholders' meeting: "The management of our national finances has improved... the current state of most of our industrial sectors is primarily healthy."

Sir Harry Goschen, the general manager of National Provincial Bank, also said at the shareholders' meeting: "I think if we recall the summary of 1932, we have good reason to say that this year was one in which our country set a good example to the world. In this year, our country restored its credit and financial dignity with a steady attitude, reduced the great difficulties encountered by domestic industries abroad, and achieved considerable results in promoting the work of recovery for Britain and Europe."

The Economist summarized its opinion of the speeches of the bank leaders by saying, "... From various estimations of the current situation, a common point can be seen, which is a firm confidence carrying some optimism." This complacent speech by the bankers triggered a significant reaction among the leaders of many large industrial enterprises. However, within a few days after the speech, the unemployment figures for January 1933 were announced, revealing that prosperity was not directly forthcoming.

The report released by the Ministry of Labour pointed out that on January 23, 1933, the number of unemployed persons registered at employment agencies was 2,903,065. This is the highest number in British history, an increase of 179,778 compared to January 1932. However, this figure does not accurately reflect the recent surge in unemployment in Britain over the past year. Obtaining an accurate figure is almost impossible, because the compilation of various statistics published by the Ministry of Labour is intentionally incomplete and conceals the actual situation. However, after a thorough review, it is not difficult to derive an accurate picture of the actual scope of unemployment in Britain. From January 25, 1932, to September 3 of the same year, 171,495 unemployed persons were deemed ineligible after being subjected to the "means test." From September 3, 1932, to January 25, 1933, another 82,331 unemployed persons were subsequently deemed ineligible. However, since the "means test" began in November 1931, more than 50,000 unemployed persons had already been denied benefits by January 25, 1932. Therefore, up until January 25, 1933, the total number of unemployed persons deemed ineligible in this way was 303,326 (of which the figure for December 1932 is estimated at 18,000, and the figure for the period from January 1 to January 25 is estimated at 12,000).

Among the unemployed persons receiving benefits, the benefits received by more than 535,637 unemployed persons were reduced by a significant amount, with the majority receiving almost no benefits. In addition, the "abuse prevention regulations" protected by the former Labour government deprived 179,888 unemployed persons, especially young unemployed persons, of any benefits.

In summary, the following facts can be derived:

Registered at employment agencies: 2,903,065. Rejected due to the "means test": approximately 303,826. Rejected by the "abuse prevention regulations": 179,888. Total: 3,386,779 people. However, there are still many unemployed persons working in economic sectors that do not participate in unemployment insurance, such as rural workers, domestic servants, and employees of freelancers. These unemployed persons also do not need to be added to this total. Not long ago, the Minister of Agriculture reported on the situation of rural workers in the House of Commons. From this report, it can be seen that in 1932, the number of rural workers employed decreased from 774,449 in 1927 to 697,120, a decrease of 77,329 or slightly more than 10 percent.

However, this is still not complete. Checking the "public assistance," the total number of recipients in England and Wales increased from 979,888 to 1,225,103 by the end of September 1932, an increase of 245,215 or slightly more than 25 percent. The number of public assistance recipients in Scotland is approximately 274,894. Therefore, there are definitely 1,500,000 people receiving public assistance in all of Britain, and approximately 3.5 million unemployed people.

In other words, there are five million workers in Britain who are either relying on the meager benefits of employment agencies or on even less public assistance. If we add the families of these workers, it can be considered that approximately 20 million workers (out of a total British population of 45 million) are living in poverty. (To be continued)

Lihuang County Officially Under Anhui Jurisdiction

After a prolonged dispute between Anhui and Henan provinces, the Bandit Suppression Headquarters has recently confirmed its jurisdiction. (Anqing Correspondence) Jinjiazhai Township, which belongs to Liu'an County in western Anhui, has been occupied by bandits for many years, and its people have suffered greatly. After the area was recovered last year, the Bandit Suppression Headquarters of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui provinces decided to establish it as Lihuang County to handle all post-war reconstruction matters. Subsequently, the question of whether it should belong to Anhui or Henan was delayed for a long time. The Anhui provincial government, citing the longer historical association of Jinjiazhai with Anhui province, repeatedly urged the headquarters to assign it to Anhui, and dispatched boundary survey commissioner Liu Yunqing in October to the county to discuss the boundary survey issue with representatives from the headquarters and the Henan and Hubei provinces. The headquarters appointed two Ais as the county magistrates to begin establishing the administration and dispatched commissioner Zheng Yangwu to the county to discuss the county's area with all parties. It was decided to allocate 17 "bao" from Liu'an County in Anhui Province, 8 "bao" from Huoshan County, 3 "bao" from Huoqiu County, 2 and a half "bao" from Gushi County in Henan Province, and 14 and a half "bao" from Shangcheng County, for a total of 45 "bao." After arriving in the county, Anhui commissioner Liu Yunqing repeatedly consulted with all parties on the issue of the county's jurisdiction. Everyone agreed that the county should be under the jurisdiction of Anhui in terms of history and geography, and they telegraphed the provincial government to forward it to the headquarters for review and approval, but an appropriate solution had not yet been reached. Therefore, Liu went to Hankou in early March to meet with Yang Yongtai, the secretary-general of the headquarters, and presented detailed maps of the county's past transportation routes. Yang indicated, "From the perspective of transportation alone, it is sufficient to prove that it should belong to Anhui. However, the Anhui province must expedite the construction of the highway from Damaidian to Jinjiazhai and ensure that it is open to traffic by the deadline, and please ask Chairman Wu to send a responsible telegram so that I can use it as a basis to request the commander-in-chief to approve and confirm the jurisdiction." Liu then left Hankou and returned to Anhui, reporting everything to the provincial government and the Department of Civil Affairs. On the 10th, the provincial government received a favorable telegram from Secretary-General Yang, stating that the headquarters had determined that Lihuang County belonged to Anhui. The issue of jurisdiction that had been delayed for a long time has come to an end. (March 22nd)

Gu and Sun Arrive in Shanghai

Song and Yu Visit Wang

I don't know when Mr. Wang has decided to meet. (Answer) After Zhaoming entered Nanjing, he exchanged telegrams with Chairman Chiang and agreed to meet at a later date. Foreign Banks Vigorously Absorb Silver

According to today's Japanese-language Shanghai Nichi-Nichi Shimbun, since the Ministry of Finance implemented the abolition of taels and the use of silver dollars concurrently, the tendency of foreign banks to absorb silver has become increasingly evident. The amount of silver exported to the United States reached 1,500 bars by the 19th. At present, American bankers such as the Mercantile Bank and Citibank are still continuously absorbing silver, resulting in the gradual transfer of silver reserves from Chinese banks to foreign banks. The silver reserves in Shanghai are also showing a gradual downward trend. As of the 23rd, the current silver reserves are 153,189,000 taels of silver and 258,990,000 silver dollars, that is, the silver dollars have increased by 2,600,000 yuan, and the taels of silver have decreased by 261,000 taels.
